Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it in the old days "contused cure," and it is that you make behind the patient who has this malady the hairs that he have on his forehead, then you make III incisions on the forehead equally according to the length of the forehead; and one of the incisions as II should all remove the forehead down to the bone, and the others II as II ribs above the cheekbones; and guard yourself from the incision of the arteries that are at the II ribs above the cheekbones; and remove your hand from the continuation of the II mandibles, and let each wound be the quantity of III fingers across; and have a piece of sponge and much of clothses for to wipe the blood, then put the sharp spatula of II parts of which this is the form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is over the temple until the second incision; and scrape all the marrow that is between the .ii. cuts at all the fascia that is above the bone, then make another from the middle incision until the other second, and then extract further this spatula
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If put in the first fissure the instrument that is called "cultellaire", and is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is blunt, not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the rib cutting toward the air side to the heart, and the rib bottom towards the bone, and the point until it comes to the middle crack. 
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head as the eyes so long as the incision is continuous until it reaches the one who opens the heart, and then another part made in the middle fissure until the other end; and then extract the blood equally, and press the place for the blood taken; then put in each fissure a tent of old cotton, and put on drapes moistened in wine and oil and basil, and keep that pus does not come; and on the third day untie the thread, and there administer great plant of water tead, then the cure of basil ointment with rose oil, and other cures which one cures wounds, as long as it is healed.  
dou reume des eulz	of the eye's
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When to any come a sharp catarrh, and you see the eyes watery and small, and weakening of sight, and the papers burned; and the hair falls out, and where chief in them make an acute pain, and the patient sneezes; therefore know by these accidents that those matters and this catarrh do not come but from many veins, and the moisture cure that is there, so is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to lay back their head, then make a deep cut in the middle of the forehead, and another along the brow. 
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begins from the fissure of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move in eating; and when the bone is uncovered, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then sew between the two lips of the fissure and put old cotton there, and linen bandages; then tie above with cloths moistened in wine and oil, and guard against hot abscess; when it is removed, it is necessary that you rub the bone until cartilage begins to grow, then cure it with drying things, that they make cartilage.  
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take .ij. parts of wheat flower, and .iiij. parts of colophony, and make a plaster from them; and administer it in these wounds to cause char to grow throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stuffing of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that which falls into the ears is one of the four things: or grains, or beast, or stone of mine or similar thing as iron; or seed, as beans, lentils, peas; or flowing thing as water and oils and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear, stone or another thing that does not join with the ear, nor grows in the ear, then put the ear to the sun. 
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, if there distill any drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and let him sneeze with condiment, and stop his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and elevate the ear above. 
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times comes pus by this cure; and if it does not come pus, administer the extraction with subtle pincers, for that is the form. 
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps forth with the pincers, that is good; if not, administer extraction with a fine instrument of small doubleure; and if it does not jump forth by this, make a chain of iron and put the head of the chain or through the opening of the ear forcefully, and stop what is around the chain with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the chain; then pull forth forcefully, for often it comes forth as we have said; and if it does not come forth in this manner, take a gut which they use to catch birds, and put into some instrument that is pointed for this purpose, and put a bit of cotton around; then press the gut on the stone or whatever it may be, and pull forth.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not follow all these things that we have said, then hasten to cut open the ear so as an abscess comes out, and spasms; and the manner of cutting it is that you first make the patient healthy in the head, and extract blood according to the measure of his virtue, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and making a small cut at the root of the ear to the fat or where it depends; and let the cut be like a moon, as far as you come to the stone, then the bone according to your power, and suck it gently with your mouth; and the care until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grains that are inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot issue, then administer i. spatula tenve subtle according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision to that grain. 
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think that the grain is wet because of the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with fine pincers and a suction, as we have said, so that the extraction be aligned.  
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water therefore that falls into the ear it is necessary for the patient to use an externment of first conditions and to open the ear with old cotton. 
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie down on that same ear where the water is.  
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it leaps forward by itself, it is good. 
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If this is not done, then many stones are taken according to the length of your finger, thin and light, and they are heated a little in the fire; and you put it on the sick person at one opening of his ear, and pull up from there with his feet, and pierce another stone through the stone that is in the ear; and do not cease doing this of stone into stone until the water comes out completely, and so it will all come out completely; and if you see it, then take a reed, and put one end into the ear, and the other end hold on fire until the reed burns down as much as possible; then make another part with other reeds until the water comes out completely, as we have said in the stone. 
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is small-bodied, like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large-bodied that one can feel it, administer an extraction with tweezers; and it is the lightest thing to remove which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the division and where we treated distillations, and the cure does not benefit, it is necessary that you look at the ear in the sun: if any worms appear, then treat them with fine tweezers, and if they don't appear, take the dog of which this is the form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above. 
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And put the most subtle chief in the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then succeed form at all the chain; do this often until all the worms come out. 
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to be set straight, so stop them with cotton wool as I have said in the ear; and if they do not come out further as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proved in the excision of worms, and you will find them treating with distillations; and if distill your oils and medicines in the ear to all this instrument, from which this is the form as you see. 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be of silver or of iron, narrow below with i. small holes, and wide above to distill; and for pressing inside the distillation i. instrument of iron well made for this, and if you see take i. razor and wrap around the tip conveniently cotton; then put your oil or your juice, and what you see of your medicines in the caine, and let the caine be in the ear; then put inside the razor to all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or at the end of the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and let the distillations be i. pock heated at the fire as it is distilled in the ear; and guard that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stuffing of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to men through the clogging of a wound, or flesh growing inside the ear, and these blockages come sometimes from within the ear, if one cannot see them; and sometimes there are i.e., a poke of pus, and it can be seen well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes from within, if one cannot see it, is of great harm in many dispositions, and in this case you should put the ear of the sick person to the sun; and look inside: if you see the opening apparent, then the work has all these spatumiles of which this is the form.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be sharp and trenchant before and behind all plain, so that it does not blister the ear; if the opening is of flesh growing or a piece of the ear, then hold it with subtle pincers, and cut it lightly, until that flesh is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if an opening is made into the ear, then take a fine and light razor and heat it a little in the fire, then place it on the body of the ear.  
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the inflammation that the patient feels greatly in the ear, pierce lightly, and keep that you do not injure the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a tent according to the breadth of the perforation, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment. 
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this with no day until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and powder on powdered vitriol; and if you see swelling in the ear, then it is necessary that you withdraw the tent and move another tent moistened in cerote which is made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding comes, then dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other cures that remove the bleeding which are or treat distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the sheet of paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This althule that comes on papers of the eyes when they are moist and are dry, it behooves you to extend them with pliers and tweezers, and the edge of a spatula from their roots; then put on their place powdered vitriol.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without it decorates, then cauterize with a fine lentil cautery, and the cauterization after the incision is worth moves; and many times they return, since nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the gristle
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times in papers come from the eyes things that seem grainy in its form and in its hardness, and for this reason this sickness is called “hail,” and is a gathering of moisture thick on the paper above and below; the work is such: take ward if the hail moves from one side and the other, and it's a light thing to know; then make the broad, then the skin each part lightly, then take it with the tweezers, and the chop. 
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it without feeling a bit of the paper, do not grieve the patient; and if the fissure is great, assemble it with a suture, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not make any force, for the healing will restore it quickly and prevent scar. 
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hail is descending down into the ear towards the upper part, so turn the paper, and being the hail to pliers, and cut it and press from one side and another; and if the paper is separated by the incision, it grieves nothing; and when the hail is cut, so leave the eye of salted water, and cure the place with that which prevents flesh until the sick be healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the grease of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	This is a type of grease that is generated in the tissues under the skin, and this happens more to children than adults, and grieves their eyes, and they come down with cataracts in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because the tears hasten to their eyes; and for this reason they lie down on their faces afterwards, and sleep on their backs, and are their tissues under their eyebrows moist that the inflammation and the appearance have covered with the exinach which opens in the eye. 
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place with your thumbs and feel the grating between them. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts his head on your shoulder; and then take one drapeil of linen, and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains exirnach from each part, then put it on top of him; and press with your fingers on one side and the other, so that the exirnach is assembled within the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture with the sharp spatula a fissure of a width, and not be more than the wound made in the vein; and make the skin in length as far as you come to the exirnach; and in more places comes exirnach from the fissure, according to the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract then a whole piece of cloth with your fingers at the outside, and turn your hand to right and left until it is spread; and guard that you do not add in the fissure, that you come to the entire spatula up to the eye, that you do not blind him.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exirnach does not open at the beginning of the fissure, so accroi a little the fissure lightly until it opens; then extract it as we have said, then moisten bandages in aisil and in water, and put on top, and strain with bands.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind grain and put it above to corrupt the moisture which is lingering. 
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the cure as long as it is healthy. 
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to a hot place, so treat it with soothing ointments until it is healed. 
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When in papers hairs grow arranged other than the natural ones, and are inflamed, they harm the eyes and bring many kinds of maladies as accustomed tears and softening of the papers and albuginea, as much as that is the cause of the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is according to .iiij. manners: or by cautery altogether fire, or by medicine ague according to this that it is before or chapter of cautery, and it is made or by incision and stitch or by caines, according to that which I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It behooves you to put the head of the patient in your healthy one, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if this is not so, there puts an needle to all .i. thread above; and let it be below the margin of the paper or where the hair grows next to these hairs, and trace .i. thread upward to the entire paper, and turn it back to the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the hairs arranged, to all the spatula cutting, from the large tear to the small one; then extract .i. thread, and put under the paper a small tent of cotton and drapery, then reign above the paper a figure of an enche, as the leaf of myrtle, and however it behooves that the figure is according to the quantity that you see raise the paper which is divided to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is one who needs it, cut a large quantity of the paper according to what the paper is soft; then make at all the spatula on the II lines that you have signed, and commence from the top great tear down to small; and let one of the slits be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the incision in one of the two angles of the ear, then peel it completely; then assemble the two lips with a suture of a needle at all the thread of fine wool, and wipe the blood, and make air the superfluity of the threads on the two eyebrows at all none gluing things, if you want to do this; and if not, take no care, then leave the suture and the threads until III days or IIII; then cure the wound without suture with dry and constricting things, because the paper revives at the bottom of the wound and the assembly of it, but the suture is changed (as the ancients said), and this work without fear; and if in another manner: and that you sign the paper with a figure which is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have counted, at III incisions separate according to the form that is here: 
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut that which rises above the small forces equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you do not have power to hold the pliers, and the thing is not equal, take a needle that has thread, and put it into the figure; and put the other thread next to the big tear, and the second thread next to the small one, and assemble between your two threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin above where you have signed, as we have recounted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by sewing, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar ointment soothing; and sometimes it happens that the hair of the paper are converted: so it is necessary that you use what we have said of the incision; but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial. 
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the splints is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and the felt inside according to those that I have said, and then make .ij. splints by art, and .ij. subtle ligaments as long as the paper and the width of the spatula are; and cut the .ij. heads of .ij. parts where you hold the threads; then assemble the one and the other subtly on top of that which overhangs the paper of the eye, and strain the .ij. splints of the .ij. parts form; and let it remain thus for some days, and the skin that is strained will die and wrinkle and carry itself, until it falls by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, if he has strength with the blow, then cure him until he is sound; and when the wound is healed, and the paper is removed, and they will not prick any longer the hairs; and this is the form of the two cauteries that you shall make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide. 
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The works is such that you prick a subtle needle, and put in it one thread of silk, soft and subtle; then assemble the heads and knot them together subtly, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then order in the chase another thread of silk, finely braided, and knot the chief of the threads; then put the patient’s head on your healthy one; and let it be in the sun so that the work is clarified, for it is a subtle and fine work, then put the needle all the way into the chase in the root of the hair adjacent, and make it pierce in the paper carefully until you draw it from above the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the chase, and put in the chase that hair, if there are one or two or three or more; then extract your hand so that the hairs come out all the way into the chase in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then you will draw the chase down to all the thread that you have ordered it, until the chase comes out of the opening above and you see it with the vision of your eye; then you will draw the chase and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair is rooted in its place and grows the flesh above; and if the hair is small, accompany it with one long hair from the natural ones, and let it be raised with that one or you leave it, until it is elongated and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the rot of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or rot comes in the eye, if there are two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural. 
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by force of a wound, or incision or cautery, and by similar things.  
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of the work in it is that you cut open that suture, and separate the lips of it, and put inside linen tents, and tie it until it is healed; and it does not behoove you to use in the cure of it things that dry and restrain. 
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness returns worse than at first; but there is work of softening things, such as fennel; and the rosehip of water or high and flax seed are cooked, and a dyacylum ointment melted in any oil, and wrap a tent, and treat it. 
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not suture according to the form that it was before; and these operations that we have said are nothing but remedies for this sickness, that it may not return according to the form that it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the char that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This sickness which is dislocation truly is called “axacrati”, and is natural and accidental. 
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the way of the work in this is that you prick an awl, in which it has the double thread, and you put it into the flesh, and you make it pierce from the left to the right, so that the thread goes into the two shoulders of the flesh; then is the flesh above all the awl, and the cut at the spatula wide. 
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what it should, it is good; if those are not, then take a razor and put it in the split, and turn the paper, and make II splits where the cost is inside the paper; and let the heads of the II slits be at the II angles of the incision that you have cut, and make an angle so that when they are assembled, the shape is like the shape of a letter that has the name 'I griesche'; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its cost is added down, from those who follow the paper, then adjust the II parts apart, and the seams with a thread of wool; then care for those that we have said about mollifying medicines, and bandages, until it is healed.  
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the ailment comes from a split or suture or cautery, it is necessary that you split a plain cut under the hairs of the papers, and according to what has been said before; then sever between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the malady, because it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters equip everything with all their power how it makes return the figure to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what is necessary for the operation and instruments in more dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the paper's
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this soldering happens to a man's eye in such a manner that the paper above is soldered with the white of the egg, and cannot move nor perform its natural workings, then it is necessary that you put the tip of a razor under the paper, and lift it up; and the being as pinches, until you cut what is attached to the spatula fine, which must not be too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient may not suffer that the spatula too sharp or bleaches the eye; and let your incision, with which you remove this assembly, be gentle, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and it is healed all of this assembly, and one does no time in the eye salty water, and the leavings of fresh water, and of coliere; then put between the paper and the eye a tent of linen, and put on top of the eye wool moistened in the white of an egg; and after the third day use the coliere and the things soudans until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the angle of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the angle is in two ways: it is nervouse and similar to one hard syfac, and another which is not nervouse, but is similar to white moisture congealed, that when one touches it with iron and one boils it panre as pinches, so one cannot; and the one and the other semblance begins towards the great tear, and crosses poc and poc until it covers all the view and all the light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then opens his eyes; and lift the paper with your hand, then coil the angle as pinches of small doubleure, and the rest upwards; then take a needle, and put on it one hair of horse, or of calf, or of ox, and one strong thread; and double the point of the needle a poc and put it in the angle, and pierce it with all the needle, and tie the angle with a thread and the rest upwards, and scar the whole hair along the side of the angle which follows the prunele and silk to the hair up to the head, then cut the remaining in the root of the tear with all the spatumile subtle and small forces, and leave the char natureil or tear, so that by the incision does not come the body of tears acostumeement; and no times is it ascended the angle only, and on the thread, as we have said; then the scar on all the spatumile souef of this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard that the spatula does not touch the fleshy cloth and break it, and that the needle is not pierced; and after the incision put in the eye a bit of silk ground, and from the collar made of litharge, and leave it until the next day; then cure it as much as it needs until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot put the needle in, and the tweezers cannot enter, many times this kind of nail is cured with medicines; and it grows as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it covered, it works the eye of the patient, and take the spatula lightly pointed according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the nail carefully, and if you see that it does not lessen and the reason hastens, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collar made of litharge and red ochre and ground silk, and stop the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same work, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is against you in the eye, like an abscess, then milk it, and treat the abscess first as hot as long as it is healed, then restart the work as before, as long as it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from the tear hurts in the eye by great annoyance, then suspend it to the armpit and cut a part and not half altogether, so that no body of tears comes; then distill into the eye red collyrium which is made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that arises on the iris
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	The eyes of some men are born sometimes red color, and covers the white and restrained on the eyelids and turns to the fire, and seems like a rose of battle; and the work is that the sick man puts his head in your healthy, then he works the eyes, and coil all that flesh with needles suitable to those, and the sustain at the force; then chops the first flesh, and goes to all chopping to the razor until the end, and keep that you do not bruise the eye during the work; and let the incision be of the spatula that we have said in the incision of the angle and as small forces by which one takes away the sebum, as the form after this chapter demonstrates it; and when the incision is completed and all the flesh is removed, then apply the oil of silkworm or you distill red coral and similar medicines corrosive, and put on top of the eye fire cotton with egg white, so that it may be assured of hot pus; and if there remains nothing, and the without the wound covers it, and you doubt hot pus, so leave the eye and treat the abscess with things soothing hot pus; then return to your work as long as it is healed, and thus do until all flesh is adjusted in the eye by this semblance.  
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless it is necessary that you apply the cure of each weak oil by nature's way; and of the accidental way, in the work of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member be suffering from this work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Blood vessels are red that are covered over the eye, and take away from sight their work and weaken the eye every day.  
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is therefore necessary that first you look if the eye, in which it is, is good, and there is no other illness except the evil eye; therefore coil in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head on your own, then suspend those veins all around according to your wisdom, and be the needles subtle double according to this form. 
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two lines by degrees in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then coil as forces those vessels subtly, and wipe the blood hour after another, until you see remove those vessels out of the eye; and guard that you do not prick the eye with the points of spatulas, and make this work at the hour of midday before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cut further than those vessels; and when you will have done this, then distill in the eye collyrium green and red for to corrupt what is remained of the blood vessel.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot gather all of these in that hour, make a plaster on the eye of things soothing the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is soothed and the abscess is sure to be hot, then begin again according to this manner which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire is called "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cautery and with sharp medicine according to those that I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is something in it that you cut on the abscess, where it should die, and treat all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, then the king has all the instruments of this form; and it is called “sharp chief,” and it is made of iron one chief point, and it is pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that this corruption is removed; and do this several times, then return the place to medicines drying.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the parts are united and flesh has grown, and the body of the bow is united, and it remains so for 40 days, and it does not heal and is not suppurating, know that it is healthy; if not, there is nothing else to do but bring back the fistula to the opening according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time by iron, and by sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered, take I forest according to this form, and let the iron head be at 3 angles, and the shaft be thinned up to the top as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it upon the bone near the tear duct, and withdraw your hand from the eye's point, then turn all the way back as far as it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through what comes into his skin if he holds his hand on his forehead; and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens in its place, the matter goes to the forehead; thus it is easier for the patient. 
de l’issue de l’oil	from the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are open fully and there is no disturbance in the nose or diminution, then you must bind the patient; then cleanse, then place suction cups or a leech without harming to suck, then place on the eye i. one linen made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocolla, and then strain the eye, and apply a plaster on it with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths soft enough, and double each one in four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye needs; then strain them from above with a hard bandage, and restart the suction cups to suck without harming; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the linen softens, then you must strain it a lot; then remove the linen after the day and the night, and if you see the eye repairing, it is good; if not; then restart the plaster and cloths and the linen and suction cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the dislocation of wool
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes in the woven cloth, then open it, and there come forth fibers like .i. grains of resin, and it is astonishing to see; therefore if you see it covered, the work is such that you put a needle into the root of the lower part until the one above, then put another needle where there is .i. double thread from the tear; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the disposition; then cut the place of the double thread and tie one part of the grape around it, and restrain it well, then extract the needle and put on top the oil-like half in abundance of an egg; and let it stay until the threads fall with the grape, then cure the eye with comforting things as long as the wound is healed; and at times the wound is restrained by the grape each side of a circle of cloth, as long as it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes show great appearance, then pierce it with a subtle spatula that comes from the oil, and correct the albuminous moisture and lower the eyes, and enter them immediately; then extract it as long as it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the  bow of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This sickness which is called "alcunnati" is nothing other than a film that is assembled in the eye, resembling water descending, and it is not water; and the manner of appearance of the work is that you make the sick person sit on the prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands from two parts, and move it until you see the film come up to your eyes; then it should be fixed, and do not descend and let the light become scattered, and the sick person sees things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the film is not arranged as we have said. 
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the subtle spatula and go on the cornea with the continuation of the conjunctive with the cornea and crown, as long as the bow emerges; and when it is out, distill into the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek that is boiled and honey, then be cured with other cures until it is healed. 
des aigues de l’oil	of the needles of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the appearances of wounds in division, and what is necessary to examine them; so operate according to health.  
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It behooves you to make the patient sit between your hands crossed, away from the sun's light, and tie their good eye and hold it tightly; then put the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument called "almagda," or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then place the tip of the instrument beside the cornea by the width of a thread in that white part of the eye to the side of the tear duct, then insert the instrument called "almagda" skillfully, and retract your hand until it pierces the white part of the eye, and feel that the almagda comes to the empty thing; and it behooves that the measure of the way almagda is at the full length of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the darkness; and this is the cornea of the eye; if you will see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the corneal membrane, then put the instrument up to where the liquid is, then express it drop by drop. 
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water descends now, the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye. 
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After rest a little, and if the water rises in the second way, put the force with the instrument, and when it is fixed and she does not rise, gently remove the almagda by turning your hand back and forth; and then put back a point of the veil gemme, and leave from there the oil inside.  
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by means of a fire the oiled cotton or wool steeped in rose oil and in abundance of egg, and tie with the sound eye. 
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put on top a coming crushed with an abundance of egg. 
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, because there are some men who have their eyes too hard, it is necessary that you take the instrument called «alberit», of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And therefore pierce the conjunctiva only, and do not make it too deep, but make it subtle then put almagda as we have said; and at the completion of the work equip the patient with the bedding ahead of time so that he sleeps on his back in the dark place; and be free from all movements, and eat light meats, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and let him be bound according to his disposition until the third day; then unbind it in this same dark house, and prove his sight, and show him some things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day; and it is not fitting that you do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you do this because the liquid rises quickly. 
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When abscesses come, that you untie the eye before the seventh day, and address those who appease abscess; and when it is appeased, then untie the sight and put upon his face a little for to cover any day, and be in that dark house.  
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then it will go out of the house little by little, and turn into its state; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case. 
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in his country they made almond pierced, to which one sucks the water, but nonetheless I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the resemblances of the forms of almonds, because those who do not know them see them; and they are properly of grain.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the head of these of this same subtlety, and the hind in three angles acute.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh upon the bone
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes are born or are made various kinds of chars, because there are some that seem like scorpions with many legs; and if there is one such where the flesh has a bad color, and if it has flesh of good color. 
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that one of these carts which is soft and not yet cracked, it behooves you to make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open his nostrils, and put the sponge on those carts, and the air out; then cut what you can hold with the sharp spatula from one side, until you know that the cart is completely removed. 
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that one cannot cover, then open it all, i.e., with instruments subtle and light, so that nothing remains; and if without a sore or abscess, then support it as is fitting; and if it are malignant abscesses, then haste and cauterize it until the blood is seared and all the pus is removed, then put on either oil or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose works and moisture comes as far as the palate, know that it is healthy; and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is flesh newly in the bone above, because the instruments cannot come to cut: therefore it is necessary that you put I thread of linen a little thick, and be moistened with hands ours, and have between each knot a space I must or less; and put the patient’s shoulder the thread in his nose at its end, and pull gently until it comes through the nose inside the mouth; and many times do thus the children in schools, and this is an easy thing for him who wants to do it; then hold the head that comes from the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and feel each one after the other, being careful as we are which are or thread. 
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do what you know that the new have corrupted that flesh, then treat the child, wipe the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it straight back into the wound as before; do this three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of flesh; and then put on the wound a bandage of felt for several days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purify the head, as oil and medicines are distilled into it: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or iron, resembling an open lamp, as a basket, and lead it so; and if you see fit, make a closed basket, and let the instruments be full for cleansing the head; and have one handle at the top for holding it when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh upon the bone
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.
