Many times at the head of the bone a sickness arises which is called "telul", and grows and becomes great afterward, so much that it is a terrible sight to behold; and for this it is necessary that you cut it at the beginning, and pull out all the bone, then put upon its place the cautery or burning medicine; and if one delays to cut it until it is great, beware if it is hard, of dark color, of poor sensation: do not touch it with iron for it is an infected abscess, because when one cuts it any time, there comes great evil to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touching, not of dark color, and you see that one can entirely cut it, then empty the patient and cut it without fear, and cure its place with things drying and restraining.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the bone is cut and sutured
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuation comes in one of these working cartilage pages, it profits little, for in some men. 
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary that when this happens to anyone, if it is seen that the wound is fresh to all its blood; and then adjust the two lips to a suture, then treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrape all the parts of their core until they heal, then assemble the two lips to a suture, and restrain them, and powder above powder of dragon's blood, and ground incense; and put on top of the powders a piece of plaster of strong or another adhesive plaster, and leave it until it comes out by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed. 
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the suture is that you assemble the solution: or by needles, as we have said in the suture of the belly; or by thread, as I have made you know.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In men's mouths happen within the lips abscess hard, seeming to grains of times, and lesser and greater; therefore it is necessary that you turn the lips, and fends upon each one, and take with pincers and cut in each part; then apply there after the incision of vitriol ground, until the blood be stanched; and then the leave of this, and cure the place with dry things until it be healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times flesh arises upon the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; therefore it is necessary that you hold it with forceps, and cut it at its root, and leave to run the blood or serum; then put on the place vitriol ground, or other restraining and drying powders; and if that flesh returns after the incision, and many times happens, so cut it a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of the deaf
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the tooth is black and yellow and green, as long as the corruption comes to the gum, and the tooth is smelly; so it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his cheeks be in your saint, and pull out the teeth or scabs appear, until there remains nothing; and thus do of the blackness and greenness, and jaundice and other spots, until they are removed; and if one removes those that are at the first reason, it is good; if those no, then re-begin on the second day and the third, until you have pulled everything out; and know that teeth need various forms of instruments to pull out, according to what the work shows, because the razor with which one pulls out the teeth outside have other forms than those that are pulled between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you take care to drain as much as you can, because one should not do otherwise; for it is a very high substance until one has no excuse to pull it out.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to be treated, it is necessary that you are certain of the tooth aching. 
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain of the patient is felt, and he thinks that it is a tooth of Saint, and makes the milk of the good tooth; and nonetheless the pain departs not from him because of this, until the evil is extracted, for we have already seen to do this to our seniors; and when you are well certain of the tooth aching, then it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth at all its.  A spatula strong to guard the gums from all parts; then he moves to your two or with tweezers subtle at the first hole and hole, until it is well loosened, then firmly he affirms the tweezers; and let the chin of the patient in your saint between your knees, and hold him well so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out further, take any of these instruments and put it inside each side gently, and move it as you did first. 
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and broken, it is necessary that you fill it with dressings, where the perforations are; and if you hold it gently with tweezers, so that it does not break when you hold it; and it is necessary to work very skillfully around the gums to dislodge the tooth. 
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And therefore be well on guard that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and return to the patient by the malice of the root more great pains than the first. 
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And guard yourself that you do not act as the ignorant healers who by their haste and boldness break sometimes a bone, and they do not bring them what we have recounted; but they cause often by the incision of those great illnesses for the roots that remain there, or by the bone that they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled, wash the place with wine or oil and salt; and if blood flows from it, which often happens, apply the place with vitriol ground; and if this does not work, cauterize it.  
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, which one must first use the teeth, are to be long points and large handles, so that they do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of thick members so that they do not bend when pulling, and be made of good iron, and be toothed to hold well.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in the breast, it is necessary that you place on it softened cotton in butter for a day or two.  
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	Until the eyes are healed over, put in the pliers which are called "algefri", so that the shoulder appears like a bird's beak; and they should be made inside like a file, and this is its shape. 
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pliers, then it is necessary that you uncover the flesh around the root, and there put the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say a spatula, because this is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be thick and strong so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out with these, it is good; if these do not, then help yourself with all the instruments, of which the forms come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument which has two prongs, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments which are in front in the shape of teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pliers, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument should not be able to break, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise masters subtle find by themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the illness show them, because there are such diseases where the old ones do not teach any instrument for the diversity of others; and if one does not break the bone or the other bones, or where it is possible, then seek the instruments that are necessary, as I have said, and help with gestures, this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well holding to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but it can hold and remove; and then restore its place with medicines suitable to this, and if there is in the bone rot, and it is small, so the king has all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body, and the form is ugly, and even in virgin women, then it is necessary that you know if the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and one cannot file or polish it; therefore, the chisel; and if it is next to the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is here, and is similar to 1 small beak, and be of sharp iron at its tip:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cope little by little in hands for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can be filed, if the file of a certain form like this is.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file used to make needles; and in filing the tooth little by little in hands for days lightly, so that it does not move until it is finished; then the plane at the end with no scratch, and if the tooth is too sharp and it bites the tongue, then it is necessary to file the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not bite the tongue nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth aches
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth is loose, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on it so that it moves without hurting, and you have cured it with constricting medicines, and it does not work; if it is necessary to restrict it with a thread of gold, because the silver thread becomes green and putrid, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see fit to guide the teeth, then take the thread and bring it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the teeth between the good teeth, if there are one or more, until you come wisely up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin again the covering up to the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and wisely, so that it does not move at all; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. 
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the wires of the file with pliers, and assemble them, and put them between the sound tooth, and put it so that it does not touch the tongue; and then let it remain as tight as it can stay, and if it loosens, or the wires break, so restrain it with another wire; let it remain and will serve thus all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the arrangement of the two sound teeth, and the two bad ones, as you see:  
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, so it is put back in its place, fresh to fresh, as we have said; and let no one interfere who is not wise and suffering, and at some time the form of a tooth of bone of beechwood is made, and it is put in the place where the deficiency is, and it is restricted as we have said, and it remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this ligament comes from under the tongue or nature itself; which is born like this; or by accident of a wound glued together; and the work is such that you work the mouth of the sick person, and have his head in your hand, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament with wide incisions, until the tongue is dislodged from its place; and if there is stiffness or hardness, and it is due to a wound's stitching, so put the awl and cut the ligament with wide incisions; and be careful that the incision is not too deep, for the artery which is underneath; and when you have done this, lift the dew of rose water and assil, or of cold water; then put under the tongue a tent of linen; and band the sick person every night, so that the place may not close. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the discharge of blood comes, then put on it ground vitriol; and if the blood does not stop, then cauterize it with the slow-burning cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with other treatment until it is healed. 
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of rusty color or black or hard, so that the sick person does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards whiteness, and there is moisture, then put down the awl, and cut it with a fine spatula, and deliver it on one side and the other. And if the blood does not stop at your work, then put on top ground vitriol until it is stained, then return to your work as long as you extract everything; then raise the cloth of rose water and of seil, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there come within the throat bumps that are called “godath,” and they are properly called the two almonds, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then take care: if it is a hard abscess of small size and of fusse color, then do not touch it with iron. 
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also to prevent blood loss; but leave it until it is mature, and then you will divide it, or it would break by itself; and if it is of white color, round, and the root is fine, have the instrument ready to cover, but first look if the abscess boils rests and is calmed. 
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore, make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his head be on your hand, and open his mouth and put the pliers between his hands, and press the tongue under the instrument, because this is the form; and be of silver or steel as fine as a knife: 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And you press the tongue down onto this entire instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the needle and put it into the almond, and pull upwards as much as you can; and pull nothing else from the tissues with it, then cut with the instrument, from this comes the form that resembles a force; and nevertheless the chief are curved, and one place the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or of steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument present, then cut with tongs, from this comes the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be trenchant on one side, and on the other side no; and when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and cold and thus, and if there is a discharge of blood, gargle the patient with water, or peels of pomegranates that are cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the wound is cleansed; then cure it until it is healed; and no time arise in the throat other abscesses than the two almonds, so cut them as the two almonds, always.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman of an abscess that was in her throat, that is to say the abscess of small size; and I had well closed the entire throat so that the woman could not expire through the conduit which was obstructed, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained thus for one or two days. 
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high raised that it had to be cut open with two incisions through the two openings of the nose. 
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I had therefore at once, and placed one incision in the middle, then drew out the pus, and drew out a large portion of pus; then I made another opening on the other side near the two incisions, and opened the mouth and pressed down the tongue; after that, I placed the knife in these abscesses, and cut into one part, and there came out only a little blood; and thus was cleaned the woman's throat passage, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew back together, and filled up the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; therefore I tightened it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it stopped growing; and I left those parts, and only know what God did to her after me. 
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When it is gathered in the eye, and it is full and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is quite large and round, it is called "eye". 
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the chapped abscess is appeased, and it is subtle, then it behooves you to cut it; and the one that is rounded assembled and is not long; and it is sanguine or of fusse color or black, then it behooves you to close the incision of it. 
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.  
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It therefore behooves you, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and its length, that you make the patient sit before the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument of which we have made mention above; then insert the probe into the eye, and pull it out, and the scoop of the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds. 
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluity that is beyond the natural term; for if you cut more, you harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed. 
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of the cut, then it is necessary that you use an instrument to the cauterizing of the senses of fear. 
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp pointed. 
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head on your healthy one, and then presses the tongue to the instrument that we have said in this chapter of cautery, and confides with a lively sharp cloth so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and in employing the tip of this instrument, for this is its form:  
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put on his head a hair or where one puts the medicine, as the handle of a spoon, and put the instrument to all the medicine above the grape; and the patient be lying on his side, so that the saliva and the muscle run from his mouth of the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the windpipe; then hold your hand to all the medicine and press it onto the grape, the quantity of half an hour, until you see it burning and the bite of the medicine is calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wet the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument to all the cotton into the channel above, until the cotton hardens on the grape; and do this often, until the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and after four or five days. And if you need to recommence the cauterization of the medicine, commence it again, and after the cauterization, wipe around the grape, with cotton dipped in butter, and cleanse what is around the medicine; and be raised with cold water, and be cured with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, nor cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calament and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, and assemble them all or some of them in one pot, and put it inside, and make it boil; and the pot should be well glued with strong earth, and within the pot have one instrument shaped according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And be it silver or iron, and let one of the heads be placed in the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the vein, until the eye is deadened; after that restart it often, until the eye dries, and keep that you do not do this at the beginning of the coming of the hot abscess, for many things happen; and do not make this except at the decline of the hot abscess. 
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a cane and put inside its head a sliver of egg so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the sliver of egg does not allow the steam to burden the mouth, and it is good cure altogether salvation. 
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it is lodged in the throat a bone or spine of fish, or any thing; so it behooves you to draw out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see move the thing; and what does not appear to you and is returned to the throat, it behooves you to make the sick person vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps if it will draw out the thing dry by vomiting; or the sick person swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or one morsel of dry bread; and tie to the sponge one thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will lodge itself, and then you will draw it out further; and if it does not come out by what we have said, then take one instrument of plumwood according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that it may more easily enter into the throat, and have the head high raised; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all come to naught, nor thrust in the bone; and move it is better that the patient thrusts the instrument, for he will know whether or not the thing is harsh; so thrust down, or draw it forth with all the instrument equally, as long as it be forth.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the bleeding of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	No times is medicine the woundless, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when those do not profit, then look in the throat of the sick person to the sun, then that you press the tongue to the instrument that I have told you. 
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the bandage, treat it with all the smallest pincers or subtle tongs that are fit for this. 
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this doesn't work, take a well-bred dog and put it in the throat of the patient, then put the tip of the dog’s fur on fire, and do this often. 
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And the patient remains with a fever all day. 
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full the cup of cold water, and open the mouth, and place it in without swallowing, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the patient feels the water, he falls. 
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then smoke the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I have said in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, because it will descend without tarrying.  
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot in which there are burning coals, and have the bottom covered with a covering pierced in the middle, and in it place the head of the instrument; then throw your fumigation in, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not go out, but comes until the nostrils; and the nostrils will now run, and if they do not run, begin the fumigation many times; and suffer the patient thirst, and munch things salty and others, and drink no water; and then it is necessary for it to be gone by this government. 
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the throat is, when it can be seen, like tongs curved so that they can enter into the throat; and it has the semblance of a bird's beak, and it has an asperity of lime, so that what it takes, it cannot let go; and see here the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscesses are, according to what memory comes afterward in this book, and they are diverse in puncture and size; and it is in two ways one of which is in its own resemblance, and that which it holds moisture. 
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the eyes where they are on the body. 
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	because the abscess of the head is other than that of the foundation, and the abscess of the fleshy part is other than that which comes in the joints, and each has its judgment in the work. 
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if to abscesses one should not pierce until the boil is mature according to its completion; and if to those it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses that are near joints. 
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and one lets it be so until it is rotten and festering, by adventure the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which is cause of contraction in that limb. 
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	If the abscess is near the main limb, and if you delay the perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the principal limb; or if it is near the base, pierce it as soon as it is ripe; and it is not fitting that you pierce an abscess without complete digestion, except for the one near the base, so that it does not go too deep, and be lengthened inside, and a fistula comes; and cannot heal in a long time. 
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of the perforation of the abscess which is mature according to its fulfillment, and that is when the pain is appeased, and the part of the fever diminished, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and the shaking and the softening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the piercing where the most dependent part of the abscess is, and where it appears to bulge; and be the piercing long in the body, and if the abscesses are on the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all their places equally where there is no crease.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these that ache, according to which member. 
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better that you let the opening remain until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said. 
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before those, then the body of the venin will be lengthened from him, and is full of much filth; and by chance it hardens the lips and the depths of him.  
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if at any abscess which are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limbs need. 
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you bring in small abscesses, small openings; and in large abscesses, large openings, and many incisions according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to shave the heart, and cover; when it is healed as well as the drapes, and is withered, then it is necessary to do as one does with buboes: and if there are some that are cut in III angles, and if there are some that are covered like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of the angers; and if there are some where one makes a round size, and other sizes and similar incisions.  
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no chief, such as a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it completely; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, if you do not draw all the pus in that hour, but drain one part; then plug the abscess until the next day, then drain nothing straight away; do this many times from small to large, until the pus is all gone; same as if the patient is of weak virtue, or a pregnant woman, or a young child, or an old man decrepit.  
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirits sometimes emerge with the issue of the bowels, that by chance may kill the patient, and you do not take care. 
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid therefore this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, so wipe the wound, and look if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a flat incision, so administer tents of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many holes, then it is necessary that you put in each one a tent so that it comes against the other; and if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin, and you have brought it together, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or lint shavings without moisture, and tie it until the third day; then the bone, and cure with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bloodletting occurs in your work, so administer cold water and easily, and moisten the cloth, and place it over the site of bleeding many times. 
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the flow of blood persists, administer government and care, and the powders that I have said in this book, and if it is in winter, and the place where the abscess is very nervous, then it is necessary that you put on tents and drapes moistened in wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer, and the place is fleshy, then it is necessary that you put on drapes moistened in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then untie the abscess and wipe it and cure it, as it is necessary, until it is healed. 
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this must be known universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	Of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where small abscesses come to the head, and are mannered like us that are in webs, as the twig of a hawthorn, and much in likenesses. 
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fat and such where there is moisture also as wrists; and there are some which are hard and stony at the waist, and there is no doubt if the artery does not go against it. 
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the waist is that you prove to all the instrument which is called "entromissoire", because its shape comes after here, what it contains. 
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, dry it from above with a long one. 
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is dried, one scrapes without leaving the hair that contains the moisture, because it returns readily when one leaves it alone; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and clean those which are remaining from the night.  
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then begin again the cotton, as before, the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain of the wound; then cure the wound with ointment as is fitting, until it is healed. 
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds in the fat, so cut according to this form, long; and put your oncines there, and the skin off from all sides, and put all your care to draw out the pus where it lies; and if the artery makes you opposite, so do what I told you after. 
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do so for the abscess if it is pus-filled, and of its cutting and curing as I have told you. 
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cutting above a pus-filled abscess and moist one is lighter because they are of little blood. 
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if in any of these abscesses or chiefs where there is no moisture, and from these fut I abscesses that I copied or chief of an old woman; and found the abscess as a hard stone, rough and white, and could not break; and if one had made any incision in it, one would have done him as well as with a stone. 
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or chief, for those which come to the chief of the children and to the roots of the ears, let the opening be always at the most dependent place, so that it may issue pus well; and treat them as is necessary. 
des scrophules	of scrofulous sores
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses happen at the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come from other places or parts of the body, and they are bad, and they are intertwined with each other. 
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofulous is properly within its side, as the new and abscess of the head, as we have said; and the resemblances of these scrofulous are many. 
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some who contain moisture, and if there are wicked ones who do not want to obey health.  
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that which you see of good disposition at the touch, and similar to the color of the body, and moves from each part and is not averse to the nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the conduit, and is not too deep; then it is necessary that you cut it from above, and scrape it from each part, and are the two lips of the heart as incisions, if you have need for it, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and treat it little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and do not be too spathe nor trenchant, so that the hands escape, and do not see too far forward, so that you do not cut what you should not. 
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put in the wound powdered vitriol, or some powders that restrain blood, and constrict the wound; and leave it until the abscesses are appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot. 
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is cleaned, return to your work, until you complete it; then, examine with your index finger if there are any small pustules, if so, cut them and remove them. 
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if in the root of the scrofulous vein there is a great one, it does not behoove you that you cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it hang by it, without nuisance; then apply the wound of old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then cure.  
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the whole scrofula, it is necessary that you assemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, because there is no longer any superfluity for the size of the scrofula. 
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	so it is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it, and draw forth pus, and cut as we have said. 
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that hold superfluity, pierce there where it opens more; and pierce thus as the one before said, in depending, then administer tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what is remaining of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, then the cure of ointment engenders flesh, until it is healed. 
de squinance	of scabies
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of cutting open the throat; but I have never seen anyone do it in our land, and this is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squint, it is necessary that the slit in the throat called "epiglottis" be cut open; and do not help them because all veins and the pores of the sick are hot at these who have abscesses in the mouth, or in the throat or in 2. almonds.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the pore, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below III circles or IV a small incision across, between the II circles or by the quantity of the incision of the syfac, not in the cartilage; and these are so suitable for the section of the epiglottis that there is no meat, and the vessels are long from it. 
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he extend the skin of the throat to the whole neck, then fends the neck as much as it comes to the channel; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then cut the syfac, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm of the channel that it jumps from the place which is broken, and by the fault of the voice; and leave the wound open a piece. 
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed for which one doubts strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound of the heart, and sew them together alone against the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says one should not do this juice until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the defect is in the lung.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore one cuts the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death; and for this command the ancients to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it has passed in III days or in IIII. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it, as long as it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.  
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took the knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the channels of the windpipe; and I was called by her to cure her, and I found her as dead. 
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had issued from it, and well that it had not yet cut a vein nor led further than the throat, and the veins were thereby brought out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I bandaged it and I treated the wound until it healed; and the lady did not have any other problem but that she was hoarse of voice, and afterwards returned to her disposition; for this reason I say that there is no fear in cutting the epiglottis.  
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called “throat hernia,” and it is a large abscess in the color of a blister, and is most common in women; and it is according to two manners: natural, and accidental; the natural has no cause. 
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident is according to II manners, of which one is similar to fat for us, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery; and there is fear, and it does not suit to work to do hard than in this one who is small, and probes and searches at all the intro. If you find it as I fat, and cannot to any vein, so cut it, as we cut the fat, and treat it at all its edge, if there is any; and encircle well soon, and cure it as it is due, until it be perfectly healed.
des nous	of ours
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways there are to us, of which I will say all the similarities; and now it is necessary that I say all the difference that is between our and exit. 
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that a lesion is sometimes feverish and hot, as long as the boiling has passed, and the putrefaction is complete; therefore rest the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the new one there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and contains the boil, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins also like a pimple, and becomes large; and they are according to two appearances, or greasy, or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division. 
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the new wound, that you first examine and inquire into all the instrument which is called "entromissoire," according to what its form will be or chapter which comes after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of probing abscesses as we do is that you prick or moisten the place that you find in the abscess, and turn your two points (and points), until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then after it be according to the size of the abscess; then remove the probe, and take care in what jumps out.  
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture runs short, what color it has, do as I have said about other abscesses; and if after the introduction no moisture comes, know that it is fat, so do it in a cross, and take it with pincers, and scrape lightly on each side and ward the coat where it lies so that you draw it out healthy with the new; and if you cannot draw it out healthy, then draw it by pieces so that nothing remains. 
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	Car if it remains nothing, it returns to us many times; and if it remains a little, and the wound grieves you, apply powders corrosive to the wound and restrain the wound, and put above soothing things an abscess of hot, and cure it with other cures until it is healed; and if the wound is great, sew the two lips of the wound, and cure it of what causes flesh.  
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein is too weak or otherwise you are in haste and apply the place of crushed vitriol, and leave it for two or three days until the wound purges, and rests the boiling of blood; then return to covering those that remain from the new.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of the introiter instruments, and they are in III ways: great and medium and small; and there are III squares that are called "albaret", and I which is called "breb", and there are also in III ways: large, medium, and small, to enclose the abscesses of fistula; and they are also like the needles with which one sews the sorceresses, and they are of citrine bronze, or iron, or silver, and most valuable are those that are yellow, and they are more proven by black pitch to enclose the fistulous sinuses; and they are in III ways: great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the breadth of the wounds. 
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the probes are of many resemblances, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are probes that have II curves of III ways also; and there are probes that have III curves, and are also of III ways; and there are probes that have II curves, and probes of a single curve only, and are of III ways; and all these are necessary in their place. 
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The chief of these are made cutting, and there are some that do not cut more than one side, which we scrape the nerves with, so one does not cut the vein or nerve; and of these instruments are the alemeles put back into handles, so that the patient does not feel them at the opening of the abscesses; and they are in three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses them only on their fleshy parts, such as legs, arms, breasts, and groin, and similar ones; and sometimes one makes the other instrument small, resembling scalpel handles, according to this form, for which one takes blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And one puts it sometimes in the place which is healthy to cut veins, and arteries, and sometimes around according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, until they seem like the breasts of women; and they remain swollen and disfigured, and whoever wants to cure them, it is necessary to follow this form from this line .b. up to .g.. 
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape the fat, and apply medicine to the wound preventing flesh, then assemble the two lips of the wound with stitches, and cure it until it is healed; and if the swelling goes down, and it softens like in women, then make two incisions in the ribs above, by two similar incisions; so that one holds onto the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. until the line .g.; then scrape the skin which is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and administer what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or because of the discharge of blood, then it is necessary that you fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it softens the remaining and fat, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the buttocks are kinds of hard scrofulous lumps or boils which contain moisture.
