Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who have moisture must be cut according to this form, from the line .b. to the line .g.: 
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, then apply the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and care with ointment after this as long as it is healing.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to a boil, then treat it as we have said for cutting boils, and if the wound returns pus, then administer cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is cut and the skin above is sewn together, many times abscesses come about, and it happens also to a vein swollen and with an abscess; and if one knows whether it is for the artery, then the abscess grows long from the cutting; and when you feel it in your fingers, you feel it strained; and when it is for the vein, it appears red as fire; and it is folly to cover this abscess, even when it is under the armpits and at the neck and in many other places, and it is very large. 
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to avoid the iron cure, and he who is at the head it is also necessary to avoid, and in that which is inflamed by an artery by raising the skin of the long; then work the waist as soon as possible, and depart beautifully the artery from the fabrics, until it is uncovered; then put under it a needle, and make it pierce up to the other side, and strain the artery with a double thread in II lengths, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the II arteries that are in temples; then point the place that is between the II links of an intromittent as long as the pus that is there comes out, and be sure to the abscess; then administer the cure that engenders bowel, until the thread falls; then cure those of ointment coming after these, until it is healed; and if the abscess is for the size of the vein, then you must hold with your hand what you can of the abscess to all the skin, then put the needle under the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and there be the double thread, so that you draw it from the other side; then tie the abscess, as I have told you, or the thread of one of II parts as II heads of the thread; and if you doubt that the threads are not going out, then put another needle to all the thread under all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and strain the threads in IIII lengths; then cut the abscess until the superfluities come out, then cut the superfluity of the keur and leave what is tied; then put on top of the moist cloth in wine and oil, then administer cures of tents and ointments until it is healed. 
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come in the artery and vein, abscesses come in the nerves when they are injured, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often to the shoulders and hips, and in all their places where there are joints, and this is a grief abscesses, and its color seems like the color of the body, and is in many dispositions without pain; and when it is restrained forcefully, the patient feels pain, and is not completely in line with the body, but below the heart; and moves well from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, neither down nor up, and the one that is in joints should not be covered with iron: for fear that there would be contraction; and the one that is on the head or forehead, makes the skin to the spatula. 
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it with a thread, and peel it, then scrape it clean and stitch the wound together, and treat it until it is healed. 
des grosses boces pendans	Of large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in the bellies and nowhere else, and it is a disease that is called "fungus" because of its resemblance to fungi, and it is the roots subtle, and the head big; and there are some small and very large; and I saw a man who had two in his belly that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and they had fine root, and they were slightly split, and oozing moisture from them. 
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them and found in one XVIII ounces weighing, and in the other VI З., and the work in the incision is that you see if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is white and moist and of subtle root; if the cope to the spatula wide, and be in your presence the cautery to the fire. 
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the waist, there often comes too great a flow of blood, and if it does not stop, then quickly cauterize; and if you see the patient is fearful and frightened of the incision of iron, take a well-made lead thread, and tie the limb as we have said, and leave it for days; and then restrain it, and do not cease to restrain the lead thread until it closes the limb, and heals by itself; and if the roots are large, be afraid to cut them all the same for the belly, but you can well cut half, then cauterize it so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and keep from cutting the tendon which is of a faint color and poor sense and milk-like.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an ulcerated abscess, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers after this.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil has festered
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from cautery of a wound or split in the skin, and is on the belly and some of the boils, as they have in other cuts, or of blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or of windiness; and if it is by the rupture of the skin and by the exit of the boil, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and opens through diverse issues. 
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is by the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it at its two sides it rises up, and then returns, and perhaps it is constricted, and grows much at the entrance of the bath and for hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, do not constrain it; and if it is due to blood, it opens by these signs the abscesses thick and hard, and are fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is puffed up to the touch, and the work is that you look whether its appearance is for the blood of the artery, or the vein, or windiness. 
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	So it is necessary that you leave the cure. 
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear in it, as I have told you in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein. 
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the boil, it befits that you command the patient to hold his arm, and be outstretched straight, then grasp all around the boil; then command him to move gently between your hands, then go around the place that you have marked with all the spatula, then extend half of the abscess upwards to the whole great incision; then bind it around with a strong thread, or a rope of strong silk firmly, and let it be new bound; then work the half of the abscess extended above the linen, and put your index finger, and seek the intestine; if you find it caught in the linen, then untie it, and put the intestine outside of the belly; and if you find the boil, then take it at the incision, and cut away the superfluity; and if the artery makes it contrary, or the vein, then go well around, then return to your work and take II needles, and put II through thread, and put the II needles around what you have done in a cross that you make appear; then strain the abscess in IIII leagues above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and let the place remain as long as it will rot, and allow the dead flesh to fall away by itself; or you cut it when it is subtle and rotten, then cure it of what is necessary, and finish the abscess as we have said; and strain the blood or the moisture that you find, then cure the place of what is necessary, and join the place. 
dou chancre	for the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the appearances of ulcers, and how one must work on them with medicines, and how one must avoid the cure of iron; and let us say that the ulcer is generated in the marsh, and great caution should be exercised in its treatment, and the ancients said that when an ulcer is in a place where it can be scraped like an ulcer that is in the armpit, and in the groin, and similar places, then one must remove it entirely when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, it is not fitting that you approach it, for I have never healed any, nor has anyone healed any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the works, when it is in place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge at any time the patient of black bile; then make him bleed if he has a manifest repletion, then prepare the patient i.e. good place to make the work; then get your tweezers or chancre, and the hair on all sides, and the bone on all sides without leaving anything; and let the blood flow out completely, and compress the place with your hand or any thing, and if the bleeding goes against you of the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the bleeding is extinguished; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the division the likenesses of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each likeness, and the cure which is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: this is only; and one must not touch iron in these II likenesses: that is to say, tympanites and hyposarche, because it is a mortal thing; therefore when you medicate this likeness of dropsy which is called “eclytes” with medicines, and the cure does not profit, look if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness than dropsy, such as coughs and solution of belly and similar things; if you do not touch iron, because there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other illness than dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must thus operate: raise the patient straight up on your hands, and the ministers press the belly pushing the water to the lowest part below the ribs, then take the espinous spatumil according to this form:  
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be cut from both sides. 
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	At the point, and nevertheless it should not be so deep that it can come as far as the intestine when you insert it, and do not let it bleed; then look if the hydropsy is engendered towards the intestines: if so, you should cut into it from below the third finger bone, slightly to the right of the sword; and if the hydropsy is due to the disease of the liver, then make the incision to the left of the third finger bone; and if it is due to the spleen, then to the right, and it is not necessary that the patient lie on the incision so that the superfluities do not flow to the weaker part; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and let it out, and lift your hand to the spatula between the skin and the syphac as much as in scraping to the quantity of a fingernail or more; then pierce the syphac until the spatula comes to the point where there is water, and this is the place for the water, then drive the water out, and insert this instrument from here which is the form:  
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a silver needle, and is of iron or light bronze, and at the bottom part it has one small hole; and on one side, three holes; and on another, two; and on another; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the form of the incision with which the scribes cut the feather. 
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top of the vein is the alemele, so that when the instrument comes to the point, it descends now onto the instrument; empty therefore half or a third part, for if you empty more than what is necessary in that hour, perhaps the patient will die because of the resolution of his spirit from the arm, or he falls faint, or he approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulses; then treat the instrument and hold the point, and it is now held by the heart that stops the opening which is on the syfac, because of this I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner; then restart the instrument the other day, if you see the patient suffering with this, and treat from the point a small quantity; do this any day, and guard yourself from following until it remains no more than a bit of point.  
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt on the patient, and give him much water, so cure him of burial or hot sand, and by sweating or bath and in the sun, and keep from drinking; and cure him with drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I said before. 
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stoppage of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	At no time are children born without a hole in the penis, or with a small hole, or with it not in its place. 
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary, then he must be able to see at all times through the very subtle spatula according to this form: 
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put where the little sharp pointed thing of bronze, and tie it and keep it thus for three days or four and when he wants to urinate, have the clamp removed, and let him urinate, and then put it back; and perhaps it is not needed because the urine that comes forth does not leave it closed. 
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He whose wound is small, if he medicates with the honey of pine as we have said, it shall widen. 
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the part in their place are blue, because none are born with it at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate before raising their penis; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot come to the glans, and this is a bad disease. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is that the patient lies often on his back, and are the head of the rod and the cup as well as the waist of a pen, so that the pierced one falls in the middle, as it should; and guard against bleeding that comes many times, and if it happens, with the sponge of those who sponge blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pimples on the rod
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these blemishes come in the rod, and it is a foul appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so it behooves you to prick them with one subtle needle, and scrape and cleanse them all, then put upon cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment; then cure it with diaficon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the boil is malignant, of bad color and painful, then you must apply cautery to it.  
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have captured it, and if the spur is in its socket, and has part within the skin and part outside, then you must remove the spur which is inside first; and when it is cured, then treat the outer part. 
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it all together, make sure the head of the stick is not pierced, and blackness and corruption come in its stick and groin; so it is necessary to remove everything that is black and corrupted, then put on top the ointment of honey and flour which is made of apple tree bark and herbs, then treat it with other dressings until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, administer the lunar cautery according to this form: 
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps with two conditions together: that is to say, for the reduction of blood and for corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then you must insert or conduct a stick into the penis, and urinate on the patient among; and when the hair is irritated at the head of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or where there is a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary that you cauterize it with a sharp instrument, until the bonds are loosened, and the head of the penis is delivered from all sides; and if it is a serious thing to consider this, then it is necessary that you cauterize it with the spatula a little bit at the head of the penis and the hair; then separate them well, and put in between them the fine linen cloth soaked in cold water, so that it does not irritate further. 
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a wound of continuous bleeding like other wounds; however, when we perform this work by our will, and especially on children, it is necessary that we make the best work, and the lightest to salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not say circumcision of their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have nothing more than what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have wanted the most part of the masters and healers who performed circumcision around i.e., in one dal, and with force, and a whole new knife; so it was the worse for them because there are two cloths, and by chance if one cuts the top and leaves the bottom one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the wound should be covered, and the pain is doubled, and in the purification which is done by the dal' it isn't assured the point of the member; and in the purification of the knee, by chance the iron escapes, and the work runs, and many times they are born as if they don't have need of purification and I have wanted.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the purification which is done with force to all of the thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, because the forces cut well just as much above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, so that the sizes are equal in all parts of the soul; but that the thread should be well stretched around the skin; and the manner of the first work is as if you make the child think, if he understands, that you only tie the thread around the member just so, and then let him jump in all ways that you can; then let him be between your hands straight, and bring back the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the member and blow or heart, and move it up until the head of the member is inside; then cleanse it well of the filth which is assembled there, then tie the place with a double thread, then tie it under one pock to the other thread; and hold it as II does by the second lieeure to the pouch and the index finger, and cut between the II threads, then lift the heart upwards carefully and move the head of the member; then let the blood come out poco a poco, because that is the remedy; and put powder on and on top of the powder I drape with a yolk of an egg cooked softened in rose water, mixed with good and fresh rose oil, and let it stay until the next day, and cure it from other cures until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces at the cleansing is this: the two heads should be held and should be sharp, and the heads are also as large as the hand equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the purification is when the kerchief inside is at the incision; therefore it behooves you to extend it to your finger so that the leaf makes an abscess; and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then take tenaculum and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they are three days and what is below the shaft is swollen, then let it be until the abscess has calmed, and lightly exfoliate it; then cut it as much as you can, and guard yourself from the part of the shaft, it will not harm him at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure then the wound of things suddenly with powder, which we have said or treated of powders, and if you cut the kerchief excessively, and it goes upward, it will not harm; cure it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is from the stone, or blood congealed, or bowel, or new flesh, or similar things that we have said in the division; and if the urine isn't released, and you see the retention for the stone which is there or neck of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be bent on his knees; and they should place the feet on the back, and extend his belly from the part above the back, and restrain the patient’s arms as much as he can; and thus is constrained the neck of the bladder to the expression of the stone upwards, for which reason the urine is released; and if it doesn't come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary that you administer extraction with all the instrument which is called "syringe", of this is the form: and be of subtle silver light, like the feather of a bird; and be the cane half a palm long, and be subtle at the head. 
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the issue of urine is that you take a double thread and tie it to the head of the wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe; and cut the superfluity of the wool and put it up to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and aubin of egg, and make the patient sit on the seat, and raise the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water; then gently put the syringe into the penis, until it comes to the root of the penis, then double the penis upwards towards the bulb; then push the syringe forward until the bladder, and the patient feels it come to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order except for that which leads or where it goes is twisted; then is the thread all the wool head and head, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it, and make correct the urine; and repeat the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is aligned. 
des maladies de la vessie	of the bladder diseases
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When sores or blood come in the bladder, or there is assembled rot, and you see it distill with sharp and medicines, so do to all the instrument which is called "clepsedre", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has III openings: II on one side, and I on the other, as you see; and the ends of the chevez so that the medicine be such that it stops the rod well without addition, if one can drain the moisture, and put out when necessary; and when you want to put your medicines in the bladder, place the head of the clyster in the moisture, and pull with the string which is inside; if you pull the moisture into the clyster, and then firmly reinsert the string inside; so the moisture will enter inside, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle clyster by which one clysterses the bladder: thus it is: 
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And is of silver or of archute, and is the shoulder higher; and below to the breast where the ligament falls; then take a sheep bladder and put in it the moisture which you see clistizing the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts forming with a double strong thread, and heat the end of that moisture on the fire; then put the head of the clyster into the rectum, then strain your hand upon the bladder to all the moisture coming out, until the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make it in a circle, and pierce it round through; then put the strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles the dal, and put inside that which you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder. 
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the manners of stone, and the extraction along with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone engendered as rains, and all the signs, and in what stone one must work with a cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it to you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder often happens to children, and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder seeming like water in its subtlety; and it appears hare-like, and causes the patient pain in his penis, and he thrusts many times, and then finishes; and after much of these jumps the foundations are formed; and it is light the healing of children until they have 4 years, and it is very grievous in old men, and is as medium to those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is lighter for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is necessary first to purify the patient by clyster, to draw out all the feces that are in the intestines. 
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often hinders seeking the stone. 
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and pull them and move them downwards so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and emerges from its high place; then make him sit between your hands, and his hands be under his thighs, so that the bladder be entirely declining downwards; then touch it and feel it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hasten now to cut above the stone. 
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall to the touch at all, then moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is an adult; and put it in its foundation, and feel for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, bring it to the neck of the bladder; then press upward with your finger, and push it out towards the place where you want to cut. 
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him that he extend his right hand the testicles upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin which is below the testicles in the part where one makes the cut; then put the spatula cutting, of this it is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make between those who are between the hams and the foundation, not in the middle but at the side of the left hip; and be straight over the stone, and your two sides are either foundation or bottom, and let the waist be like a travers so that it is wide on the outside, and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, and not too large; by chance the press the sides which are foundation or bottom, that it may burst without labor; and know that there are some stones that have angles, and margins: such is good to be issued; and if there is one that is rounded, like a gland, and round, whose issue is light. 
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	To those who have an angle and margin, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, it is necessary that you pull upwards with the pliers which are like a file at the top, in order to extract the stone so that it does not escape; or you put underneath the instrument subtle curved at the top; and if you cannot manage it this way, then widen the hole of the opening, and if it is not clear, then tighten the vitriol; and if there are more than one stones, first put the largest one at the neck of the bladder, then cut upwards, then pull out the stone, and the smaller ones afterward if there are many.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it must be treated, and make a larger wound. 
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For the two things that happen to the patient: either he dies or urine comes out through the place where the veins cannot join together; but nonetheless, you make an effort to drain it or break it with pliers, until you draw it in pieces; and when you have finished your work, apply incense and aloe and dragon’s blood to the wound, bind it tightly, and put a soft cloth on top, soaked in oil and wine, or in rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then bandage the patient on his neck and do not untie the bandage until the third day. 
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you unbind it, wash the place well with oil and water, then treat it with diaphania ointment and basil oil, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if boils come in the wound and corrosions, and blood clots in the bladder, and by this retention the urine is known in such a manner that without jumping with the urine: thus do you then in the wound, and extract that blood, because if it remains there, it will corrode the bladder, and it will burn; then raise the wound of water and of aisil and of seil, and help him in all the ways that you know, until he is healed; and it behooves that all the hours that you cure him, that you tie his two thighs, and assemble the medicines on the spot. 
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is where the urethra leads, and it is fixed inside, and the urine cannot flow out; so the cure of those that I say thus, that you cut it many times, there are excuses for cutting by this cure. 
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proved this thus. 
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one piece of iron in this form and be it at three angles, fastened into one piece:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft below the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then thrust the forest into the shaft lightly, until it comes to the stone; and turn the forest in your hand at the stone point by point, until you can feel the stone on the other side; then shortly will come the urine, then press your hand on what remains of the stone which is inside the shaft. 
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is then broken, and thrown out with the urine, and healed for the patient; and if you cannot do this because of any thing that forbids it, then tie one thread under the stone and the other above, then make the rod go into place the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and untie the thread, and purify the congealed blood that is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed. 
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that stone is engendered in women, and if it happens at any time, it is the cure grievous, and is forbidden for three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is one cannot find a woman well knowing who undresses herself to the mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the woman's stone is more deep than the man's stone, so it is necessary to make a deeper cut, and great fear there is. And if necessity demands this, it is necessary that you find a midwife well knowing, and with pains she is found, and if you do not find one, then it is better to cast a mirror subtle; and present her a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command of the examination of the stone; and look well that the woman is a virgin: therefore it is necessary to push her buttock or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, then she confines it below her buttock, and recommends her to push her buttock or con the patient, and seeks and presses her left hand on the bladder form. 
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, then it is necessary that she moves it from great to small from the entrance of the bladder until below, as long as it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut above the stone in the root of the thigh opposite the middle of the cone, where it is seen appeared, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move its two above the stone or below, and let the tail be first small; then put the loin in the loin, if you feel the stone so near the wound as long as the stone can issue forth, and know that many kinds of stones are: that is to say, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and which have reins. 
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the likenesses to know the outcome. 
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the stone has not yet come out, then put ground vitriol on it and hold it for an hour until the stone is discharged; then return to your work, as long as the stone is gone, and have the instruments that I told you about for extracting the stone from men to help you in your work; and if the stone has not yet come out, and it is the artery that has been cut, then put the powder on the wound and hold it with bandages and don't start again this one, and leave the stone and do not draw it any more, for fear that the patient may die; then cure the wound.  
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided, and the parts are healed, then return to your work, as long as the stone is loose.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white syfac, which is under the heart of the testicles, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac", and at times it is properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks that it is i.e. another egg; and it is the skin of the testicle between the white syfac that we have said; and these do not have this point no.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramice is so weak that it comes to the testicles, and that matter is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: either declining to jaundice, or red, or black, or aqueous white, and this happens more; and these are the signs of knowing this assembly, because if it is white as we have said, then the abscess renews, like long as the shape of an egg, and does not open the joints, because it has moisture all around. 
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture in the proper cloth, then the abscess is redden with part of the egg, and for that reason one thinks that it's another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the scrotum and the white syfac, then one feels it well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, it appears to the whole intromittent quarrel, because its form is beforehand.  
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this therefore which comes after the introducer, judge of this which is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to his strength and the fullness of his body; then lay him on his back, on a thing a little high, and put under him much of cloth; then sit on his left, and command the minister that he sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the heart of the joints; then take the spatula, and cut the skin of the joints among them long up to below the elbow, and let your cutting be straight dividing the skin of the joints until the white flesh, and the peel subtly according to your strength; then pierce the white flesh full of water at the large opening, and extract all the water, and then put your pins, and extend the white flesh upward; and do not touch the heart of the joints, but only the white flesh; cut all or in pieces even the bone of him subtly, that if you do not cut it well skillfully, it will return the water; and if the work is good in your hand, then put it back in its place when you have finished the work of the white flesh; then assemble the two leaves of the heart of the joints to a seam, then cure it as other wounds, until it is healed. 
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the leaf corrupted by another illness, then it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspensory, fearing the outflow of blood; then cut the coion at all the suspensory, and draw out the leaf, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the wound is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; so cut the other part as you have done the first evenly, then wipe away the blood, and put in the fresh wound half-soaked in rose oil; and put on top another wool piece soaked in wine and oil, and place it over the two piles, and put double cloths on top, and tie it up with all the linen according to this form: 
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and use them of wool fleece according to this likeness, and let them be assembled by sewing in the groin of the breeches, and one of the ends prick over the foundation up to the back, and the other at the part of the armpit; and the other two chiefs above the two shoulders, and let all assembly the restraint in the buckle of the braier; and once is medicine this ramice of cautery in place of a knife of iron, and it is that you prick the knife-like cautery, and cut the skin of the testicles, and be scorched as we have said, so that the white syfac that contains the water is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that syfac at once, and scorch it with this subtle cautery hot: 
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cop in all ways that you can, as long as you reach everything; and guard that the fire does not touch the eye; and know that this work is more salve; and moves guarding from a decrease of blood, and moves that the works of size; and if nothing makes contrary to you, or abscesses or decreases of blood or another thing, so cure what makes contrary to you, according to what is said before. 
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to endure this work because of its horror, then administer a perforation as I tell you, and it is that when you are well certain by the signs that we have said that the watery root is there, then make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below with all the spatula wide, and put the perforation deep into the body; and let the opening be wide so that all the water flows out; then put cotton on the spot, and tie it up, and leave to drain the remaining water, then cure it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to flow out of the mouth of the wound, then you must put a pen or the instrument with which one treats the water of the hydrophics, of which the form is before; and widen the opening of the wound, and know that the water returns, and it is assembled after six months or until then, and when it is assembled as before, and so will the patient pass his days. 
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the genitals
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the section of this branch there is fear in many dispositions, for which it seems to me that one should leave it; and I will tell you the work and appearances of the abscess. 
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come to the body, and also to the genitals; and it is by many causes.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to know by superfluity sour and ague, which is spread to the joints, or by percussion; and is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and finds no pain, and is a grievous abscess; and by chance are some abscesses grievous painful and stony, and of livid color, and sometimes comes from our artery, or from swelling of vein. 
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When this is by way of artery, it is known by the arrangement of hot abscess, when you press it to your hands; and it is not fitting that you touch it. 
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made of the inflation of vein is known by his disposition to the expression of the touch of the two, and can well make the cut on this resemblance, and on the other charts; and that you cut the heart of the coins, then being the egg on high, and the train farther from the white syfac, and deliver the suspender from all parts of the egg. 
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already hard with these shells, then it behooves you to draw the egg and cut it; and if it is in the yolk, or in what is inside the vessels, then it behooves you to deliver all that membrane and roundly cut it. 
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the cartilage is or its back, it behooves you to cut it all and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your works are accomplished, then apply the wound of wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the genitals
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a covering resembling the yolk of an egg, with the softening of the boils, and the patient cries out when he goes; and the treatment of this disease is as dangerous as before, nevertheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on the raised seat, then put the suspender of the testicles down to your feet, over all the vessels that are near the penis, and tie them with strips, and stretch them; then cut with a sharp spatula wide through the middle of the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then peel from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries which are in temples; then insert a needle where the vein has come out, and tie it at the first place where the vein has arrived, and tie it directly to the other end; then cut them in the middle straight, according to the length of the body, and extract the corrupted moisture; then treat the wound as with others where one injures the bow, so that no vessel is left that could nourish one of the testicles; for by this, no evil comes, and if to all the vessels blood comes, it is necessary to drain the testicles at all the vessels; so that the veins do not lose their nourishment because of the incision of the vessels, and dry out and cannot be healed. 
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the shoulder
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The events of this branch are by the section that comes or therefac, or the extension on the belly in the part of the angles, because intestine descends from that rupture to one of the sides; and this rupture is either at therefac, or of the extension of it, and these two manners of mouth of causes: or of percussion, or of leap, or of braire, or of lifting heavy burdens, and by similar things; and the signs when it is of the extension of therefac, is that they have pain and pain, in long time, and does not come suddenly; and are the abscesses even up to the navel, because the therefac presses on the intestine. 
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section of the syphac that it brings sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscess appears diverse, under the skin close, and this for the issue of the intestine and the body to the outside of the syphac.
