Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines are caught with it, and are held in, and cause great pain to suffer for the patient, even when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron there is fear, therefore it behooves one to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the work is that you command the patient to return the intestine to its place within the wound if it can enter; then be careful on his neck between your hands and lift the hips; then bring the heart upwards, and cut all the skin of the buttocks long; then put inside the folds of the waist needles according to what you need for opening the wound, and such that the eyes may exit; then scrape the syfac which is below the skin of the buttocks, until the white syfac is uncovered on all sides; then put your index finger into that which follows the buttock, in that which is between the white syfac which is below the skin of the navel, and the second syfac, and depart from what is behind the navel, and between the second syfac; and then move with the right hand into the heart of the buttocks, and hold the white syfac high in your left hand, and lift the navel to all the syfac towards the waist; and command the minister that he extend the navel upwards, and untie what is behind the ligament; and inquire with your two hands if there is any intestine enveloped or white syfac hard, and if you find any of these things, put it into the belly below; then take a needle which has a thick thread made of X threads, and put it in the back part of the syfac, which is after the skin of the buttocks; after the waist, then cut the hairs that appear from the threads, until there are IIII threads; then assemble them one on top of the other in the manner of a cross, and tie the syfac, of which we have said which is below the skin of the buttocks, with a strong thread of II parts; then envelope the hairs of the threads, and tie them together of II parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter inside, except an abscess should come there; and put straight the thread according to the first long thread II two of it, and after these II threads leave the syfac which is below the heart of the buttocks the greatest of a two; and after all the other according to the roundness that the egg carries; then cut in the part which is below the skin of the buttocks, as much as the sinew, and the bow, as we have said before; then administer wool moistened with oil, and put it into the wound, and put the thread that we have said. 
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never once is the white part of the face (the shoulder) that we have said cauterized after the incision, out of fear of blood loss.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, and leave the linen until it dries by itself; and if it delays in drying, let it be raised with hot water, and put on as we have said, until it dries; then cure the wound with other remedies, until it is perfectly healed. 
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I never saw anyone who dared to do the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancient ones said that it is made like the branch which is assembled with the vis, in such a manner that you tie the vessels, after the cut above or lightly below; then cut in the middle, and cure the abscess of those who work, as long as the vessels flow; and cure it as we have said, until it is healthy.  
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	No times comes rupture in the bowels, as we have said, and opens the wounds; and do not send any of the intestines to the anus, and if it does, it is little, and repairs all hours; and still, if it remains too long in this point, so it grows the wound or abscess, as much as the intestine sends out; and this happens by the extension of the abscess which is in the bowels, as we have said, because it is extended, then is softened and inflamed the wounds and opens; and the cure is like cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes is cured by iron in this manner: and that the patient lies flat on his back between your hands, then cut the wound inflated of the large size according to the quantity of III fingers; and then extract the abscess which is under the skin that it follows, then take the thread and put it on the place appearing of the abscess; and press it at the bottom of the belly, then sew the II appearing wounds of the abscess upon the top of the thread, and sew one and the other; then extract the head of the thread, and do not cut the abscess nor extend the wound or anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the root of the intestines; then the cure by the cure of the wounds.  
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, disinfect it and care for the wound until it is healed. 
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The fig is constrained, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is moved to this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times is softened the skin of the testicles in certain men, because those which are inside are softened, and it is made to be seen; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and one cuts the skin which is softened on the natural skin; then assemble the two lips with a suture, and if you see, first suture the superfluity of the softened skin with three or four sutures firmly; then cut between the sutures, and cure as the other wounds, until it is healed, and throw away the thread.
dou chastrement	of the tightening
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that chastisement is commonplace in our law, and for this reason, it would please me not to speak of it in this book; and it is necessary only for two reasons: one is that the wise ones should be able to answer when they are asked, and know the cure; and the other, because we often need the chastisement of some beasts to aid us, such as goats and sheep and cattle, and other beasts. 
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that cauterization is done according to two manners: or by attraction, or by cutting. 
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by traction, make the animal sit in hot water, until the tendons are softened and pliable; then taking them in your hand, hold them until they are put back and you no longer feel them. 
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	From the chastisement of size: it is necessary that you hold the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspender, and cut on each one with a blow, when you have well scratched them; and leave no prick of the syfac and the subtle syfac that is on the vessels; and this manner of chastisement is more mature than that which is done by attraction, because at the attraction it may happen that nothing remains from the testicles, because of which the beast desires lust; then cure the wound until it is healed. 
des hermofrodites	Of the hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is according to two manners in men: one way if between the two sexes it opens as much as the figure of a woman, where it has hair, and sometimes in short the urine. 
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is so in women, and it is on the hip as well as a rod and two points. 
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the care of man and woman is that you cauterize all the adhered sores, and treat them like other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine leaks through the skin of the genitals, there is no treatment. 
de la tentigene	Of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tendinitis is a hard knot attached to the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as big as a hand, and that is the cure.  
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you remove the superfluity of the tendon with your hand or tongs, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep, lest bleeding occurs; then treat the rest until it is healed; and for another sore that arises at the mouth of the anus, and the temple, and perhaps jump out, and is according to the semblance of a cow, and for this reason they called it by the ancients "disease of the cow." 
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary that you cover it, as we have said the bandage, and the care until it is healed.  
de erratique	of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	 Erratic it is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the opening is small; and is natural by birth, or accident by illness that has come to be; or it is by cartilage joined, or by subtle or thick syfac, and is made in the belly, or in the ribs, or below, or wherever; and prevent conception, and pregnancy, and perhaps the flowers to have; and the knowledge of this is by the regard of the bailer. 
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the stoppage is near appearing, so whether it be to your two or to the right. 
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is the subtle disease, and it is close to the two books, then hasten, and say this: put your two finger indices together, and the woman be on her back, spreading her legs; then as the two books form, until the subtle disease is round, and be over the swelling; then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and put it on the place, and lay the woman down at home each day, so that she cannot stir. 
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the sty is hard and thick, then it is necessary that you cut it with the spatula seeming like a myrtle leaf. 
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the stomachache is of flesh origin, then suspend it to the bed and the bandage; and apply blood-thinning medicines like dragon's blood, incense, along with a bit of egg white; then administer a large poultice of flaxseed so that the wound can not close; and thus be prolonged, and administer a linen tent of dry linen; then be treated with other treatments until it is healed. 
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marrow comes new flesh, if it is necessary to cover according to this manner, if it isn't festering abscesses.  
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess festering which is in the flesh, one must not touch with fire. 
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without customary treatment, and when hemorrhoids are old they become tough; and we have said in the division the similarities of those, and the signs, and I will say here those which resolve cure. 
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and boils, when they are swollen in the marsh, and do not appear to smell, except for the cure by iron. 
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the marshes, one can feel, are those one can cure.  
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you place the woman in a cold house, then the head of the bed with pliers, and the cap at its roots, then powder on medicines restraining blood, such as acaice and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then put her feet to the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding comes, then make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and willow and similar things, and then take barley flour, and confect it with honey and oil, and apply a plaster to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he endures it, it is good. 
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If this is not the case, if to him applied leeches on his back and breasts without hurting him; then take wool, and moisten it in juice of plantain or in juice of elder with old wine, and apply it there. 
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess heals, care for its place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called “albathir” is red, and is similar to the sharp chief, so it should be covered as I have said in the previous text; and then the care until it is healed. 
des apostemes de la marris	Abscesses of the flesh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many ways of abscess come in the marshes, such as chancre and purulent abscess and herpes and boils and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and more other illnesses that I have said in the division. 
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary for me to say in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the marsh, which is not like other abscesses; and if you want to know the work of iron, then see if the abscess is raised at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it. 
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore, do not hurry to pierce it, but let him suffer until the pain is eased; and then make the patient sit on a seat, and have small seats where he leans, and support his back and assemble his feet to parts away from the leg; and let his hips be spread, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good band; then pull him gently towards the right side, and there administer the instrument which works the mouth of the jaw, so that what comes after will show its form; and it is necessary when you see to administer this instrument that you put the point first in order to know the depth of the jaw, so that what enters into the instrument does not go further than it should, and that it does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then it is necessary to cover the depth of the jaw with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm him; and it is necessary that he put the cone of the instrument on top, and that he holds the instrument.  
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and one wipes it with a soft hand, it is necessary to cover at the top with a spatula, and when the bowel is empty, it is necessary that you put in the wound tents moistened in rose oil or green dry oil; and put the tent further from the wound to the edge of the ridge, and put outside on the ridge and on the pointed cotton swab wet with water or malves be boiled; then cure after II days of ointment coming to this, until it is healed; and at any time raise the ridge and the wound by a clyster of water and honey, and then with water or roots of lilies and arnica long be boiled; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is placed back into its socket, then it behooves you to guard against iron cautery, but treat it as we have said in the division. 
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is first necessary for the midwife to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs when you see the woman pressing downwards, and desiring to smell the air: then she hastens the child to come forth with force; therefore, you know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and it is the head first, and the second follows after; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press her belly so that the child comes quickly; because when it emerges from its head, then the second follows after, and it is cleaned of its superfluities by good purification; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it comes sometimes on its feet, and comes to force the body or the shoulder, and the hands, or where it comes on its belly, or groin, and is converted by chance on its neck, and by other bad figures; so there is need for the healer that she be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must help them. 
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes upon its head by natural birth, and the woman is in labor and giving birth hard, and the virtues of it are weak, then have her sit on a saddle, or let the women hold her; and rise its nature of oil or fennel seed that is cooked, and then put the midwife between her thighs with the little spatula which here is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And split the secondine, and cut at its nail until the moisture that is within it flows out; and take the belly of the woman so that the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to enema the woman with musk mallow with sesame oil; then make her cough and sneeze from condiment, and hold her mouth and nose an hour: thus now the child will be born. 
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out, it is necessary that you put them gently in and out; and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on the seat, and raise her feet up; then take the seat off the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall when taking it down; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut the hands with the knife that is placed in front, and extract the child, and put them back in evenly.  
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the issue of the child on his feet 
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes upon his feet, it is necessary to push them upwards; and then turn them back and forth, until they are even; then grasp his feet and extend them back and forth. 
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	He jumps until his hips if he is commanded to take it, and then causes him to sneeze by condition; if it is stronger, God wills it. 
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, turn it back and forth, until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is lightly.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come forward as we have said, then take a mixture of althea and sesame oil and melted gum, and grind all in the mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit in hot water up to below the ribs; and when she is softened below, make the collar of myrrh and put it below, and leave her for an hour; then make her sit on the seat, then make her sneeze and restrain her mouth and nose, and take her belly lightly, because the child jumps now. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the exit of the child on his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, he puts his hands foot and foot; then let him be laid on his neck, and let the feet hang down, and let him lie on the bed; and bend his hands foot and foot, and then takes his hands above the belly, and removes the cushions below, until she is well prepared down; and if the child does not jump, he takes his feet and moves them, then moves the belly up, then puts his hands; and move the child foot and foot; and command the woman to hold on as long as the child rises. 
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the issue of the child who comes out with a wide hand
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to try to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, have the woman rise and walk; if she cannot walk, have her lie down on her bed and spread out her legs; then administer the poultice that I have recounted; and if she does not give birth, have her sit on the stool, then try to bring back the hand; and guide the child according to its natural figure, and make her sneeze, and command her to suckle as long as the child is breathing. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the delivery of the child on his neck, and have his hands spread out, and his face turned toward the back of his mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the patient keep his hand, then turn it back and forth, and the eye lightly; and when it is equalized, he puts on the nature of muscle padding of altee and oil, as we have said, then he commands her to move back and forth; and when you will have done this, he makes her sit on the seat, and commands her to grasp; and she sneezes. 
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In this same manner to all the spine
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to this manner for the whole secondine, if the secondine is struck at its fingernail until the moisture is emptied; and if the child can stand on its face and neck, then strike the head so that it is not held back, and make the child die; then put the child inside until you have put it as it should be, and command the woman to refrain from doing anything; therefore, it will come out easily. 
de l’issue des gemelz	from the separation of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things, and do not live at all, if they can be named; I know these, that they are multiplied, and are separated by the syfac which devises them, which is tied to the boude; and sometimes they come out as naturally as one of all others, as we have said.  
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue violently, so the cure as we have said, and let the bale be subtle, and do quickly and lightly what she does; and do thus as it is worth to heal. 
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	At no time are they formed in the marshes I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of their glorious sage, and it is necessary that the bailiff knows all this, because by chance seeming things happen; so do according to what is necessary.  
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of the dead child or belly, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with your hands; then it is necessary that you know if the woman is of healthy virtue, and has no accident, or she has fear of death; then it is necessary that the woman be sustained on her back, and her shoulders inclined downward, and her legs raised; and the minister holds the cloth from two parts, or she is tied to the bed so that she does not move in the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils with wool of altea and fenugrec and linseed, then anoint the hands with these oils and these wools; then put them in the womb lightly, then desire the place where she puts the tools to be suitable to those, and take ward if the child is appearing that it descends on its head; then put the tools in her eyes or in her neck or in her mouth or in her palate or below the beard or in the forcele or near the ribs, and if the descent is on the feet, then you put them or pierce and at the mid-ribs; and it is necessary that he holds the tool in his right hand, and puts the curve between his thumbs of his left hand, and puts it to his whole hand lightly, and puts the tool in any of these places that we have said, until it comes to the void thing; and this is the form of the tool: 
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	then put one against the other one, or the third if you need it, so that the extractions are equal; and then the two in equal movement from side to side, so that they move smoothly, and let the instruments be toothed so that they hold firmly, as is shown here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if some remains of it, anoint the area with some of its oil, and place it in that part, and draw the other part; and if none remains, put this ointment or higher up there, and do this until it comes out completely.  
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes forward from the other, and it cannot be brought back by constriction, then you should wrap it in a cloth, until it is all straight; then cut at the joint of the palm or at the knife, and thus you must do with the other hand, and as for the feet. 
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's hip is large and it is obstructed at the exit, or if there is a sharp head assembled, then you must put the pointed spatula between your two hands, and make the head and remove the sharp; or you shall wrap it with the instrument called “almidach,” because its form comes with the instruments or chapter which is after this one; and in the same way do if the child has a large head naturally; and then draw the bones with pliers, and if the hip jumps out and is strained by force, then split it, until the moisture that is in or worse exit; and if it cannot issue, then cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is inflamed in the belly or under the ribs, then you must pierce it until the moisture runs. 
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the traction is light, and the application to the mouth of the well is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is entrapped in the belly or breast, it behooves you to extract it with the drapery wrapped around your hand; and make the belly or breast, as long as the moisture that is there is corrected; and if the other member is removed, and the head remains, then put your hand into the opening of the wound; and pull it out until the mouth of the wound; then put in the twine or thread, and pull forward; and if the mouth of the wound is narrowed because of a hot abscess that has come there, then it does not behoove to work it, but rather administer moist and fatty things; and apply plasters, and soak with softening and moistening water. 
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on his side, and you can put him straight, then administer what we have said in the living child; and if one has no power, then treat the body by parts, and leave nothing of the second part. 
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if they are administered the things that we have said about abscesses, which come in the marshes; and if blood comes out, it should be put in vinegar restraining, and administer other cures to them. 
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly one fetus had been killed, then conceived another on top of it, and refused death to the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, it came an abscess in the belly, and swelled so much that it opened, and began to great suppuration.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I pondered long, and could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and out came one bone, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was amazed a great deal because this one whose belly has no bone.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I touched the wound, and in between the bones of my hand, as long as the woman was in a better state; and I watched the woman for a long time like this, and it would come back a little bit from its place; and I have not recorded this chapter except because when the master finds something strange, he should know how to help. 
dou ramener la marris a son leu	how to bring the bone back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here after comes the form of the pressor, which we have in the books; and to two turns at two joints of the two limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more subtle of the restrictor, and be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the tube I do to wide, and the edge of the trees I must, and long one palm and a half; and between the two limbs be two adjustments of this same tube, which are fastened in one and the other, of half a palm long or a little more; and these two adjustments are put into the mouth of the handle to open when turning the two horns. 
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, in its appearance more subtle and lighter, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of pliers; and it has two jaws with adjustments, as you see, an arm's length long, and two palms wide; and when you see opening the vagina with the whole instrument, have the woman sit on the bed, feet hanging and legs open, then put the two attachments together in the vagina, and hold the head of the instrument below between her hips; then work your hand on the whole instrument, as you have done with pliers equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the vagina, until the girl does what she wants. 
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument are all surmounted, and are multiplied their likenesses; and when the eyes have seen them appear, so much is more hasty the work, and higher to men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise the instrument that you have not appeared it, because their necessities are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is retained in childbirth, it is necessary that you command the woman to retain her leg, and then have her sneeze with force, and hold her hands at her mouth and nose; and if she jumps because of this, well is it. 
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If it does not, take an earthen pot, and make a hole or cover in it, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as calament, rue, anise, chamomile, cassialigne and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, be cooked or boiled in water over the fire; then put a band or opening of the pot, and the other chief in the mouth of the marsh, and tie it until the vapors come inside the marsh; then make it sneeze, as we have said. 
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondine is jumped upon suddenly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this cure, and is not further healed, command the bailiff that she moisten her left hand in sesame oil or in alum ointment, and then put it into the nature, and desires the secondine. And when she has found it, seize it and extend it little by little straightly, so that the marrow does not fall to the extraction; but it is convenient to move it gently to the right and left, and then pull; if it will come and disengage itself.  
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the mare is too narrow, we have said the cure of sneezing, and fumigation of herbs; and if it is not from all that we have said, then guard that you do not use milk; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the mare, you tie it to the hip of the woman, then clisterize with ointment tetrafarmaçon; so it will bear and return, and come forth; but nonetheless, when it bears if there comes bad odor to the stomach and head, and the patient becomes pale. 
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore it is necessary appropriate fumigations for those: none of the ancients have experienced fumigation of cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument for fumigating the woman at the time of childbirth is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is to be seen like a dog, and one puts the head subtly in the nature, and the shoulders wide above the fire; and let there be fumigations on the coals, and the tinder as long as it is burned, and restart another. 
de percier lou fondement	to examine the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, but it is stopped by a subtle syfac: so it is necessary for the midwife that she pierces that syfac to its due, and does not pierce it with a sharp spatumile, and guards the lacement so that it does not touch; then puts on linen half-soaked in wine and oil, and then the cure of ointment until it is healed. 
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it does not re-stop, then put or pierce a cane of plomb, and leave him for many days, and be removed when the child wants to go into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this stupefaction comes from a closing of a wound or an abscess; so it is necessary to cover that closing; if it is cured, as we have said about the cautery of lead.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from below the foundation are nodular, and those that come from near the outside of the foundation or in the space between the two parts, if there is a fistula or more; and when this nodulation is old, it works, and still moisture comes out white or subtle bows, and sometimes these fistulas pierce; and they are known by those who have them either by discharge or venting when the patient defecates, and perhaps in leaps some. 
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if fistulas that pierce up to the bladder, and up to half of the penis; and reach up to the junction of the groin, and up to the root of the thigh.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula piercing to the foundation, and not piercing: and it is that you thrust your right index or foundation, and thrust a fine needle of lead or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting. 
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is a curvature, then put a tent of fine lead or horse hair, until you feel the tent or hair at your fingertip; and if you do not feel it, and there is no discharge or venting or ver, as we have said: know that it does not pierce; so hasten to cure. 
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced to the bladder or to the passage of urine, so that urine flows out, and cannot be stopped by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced up to the joint of the hip, then the tendon comes up to its place; if there is no twist and the invention of pain around, then it is that it is there bowed, and it does not value medicine or treatment by ointment; and in these fistulas passing there is no cure but labor, and vanity of fools' mirages who intervene in them. 
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one who is neither very young nor very old, there is hope for healing with iron, as I have experienced, and that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and lift his legs up to his hips, and have his hips inclined to his belly; then put a tent of grain, or of plank if there is tortuosity, as far as you know where the tent comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it near the foundation, then you must put your index finger there, and feel if he senses the pain; and be discovered or you feel between your finger the sinew or the flesh, then know that it is pierced; if you do not work on it a little one cannot heal it.  
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One says all things well it can be healed by this one, but it happens rarely; and the help that one does to it, if one scalds the subtle cautery according to the breadth of the fistula as it is said before; and throws it whole hot into the fistula, until it comes near the foundation; and make this two or three times, as long as you know that these charcoal are burned which seem like an eye feather; and then the cure of tents moistened in butter, as long as those chars issue out; then the cure of ointment inciting cartilage and joining. 
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healthy, that is good.  
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this is the case, it cannot be healed otherwise; and if it protrudes between, and does not pierce to the point which is the foundation, and between your two parts and the protrusion a thick covering of flesh or silk, and you see the fistula at this following the covering from the heart; so cut from the beginning of the fistula, and thrust forward ahead of the protrusion, and then the cautery after, until it comes to the head of the protrusion; and will be delivered the protrusion, and will fall away; then carefully remove those tissues that seem like an owl's feather, and nothing remains.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood flows continuously, and goes between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery assembles two good things: that is to say, the burning of these joined bones, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture; then the cure of wet tents in butter or in ground herbs, as long as the wound lies open, and if the bone has been burned within the wound; then cure the wound of swollen eyes by applying hard dried medicines. 
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes just to the bottom of the foundation, and is separated from the body, then put your finger or foundation in it, and inquire about it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and there is the cloth or the syfac or chars, where it is near to piercing, if there is no other way except the way of faith and hope, by the administration of one of the three ways: or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can put tents and cure it as first; and do not go too far in parfont, that you do not cut the tenement which holds the foundation, and let the egestions come by the desired sense; then the cure, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and the mund as soon as it is cut from its foundation, or by tent or by another appointed instrument; then mundefy that char fautree which is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to remain the fistula in the part outside the foundation: it will be a lighter thing for the sick. 
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this manner: and when you place the tent in the fistula, and it is or lies along the base below the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the head according to this form: 
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And it puts one thread twisted in two, and puts the tent to all the thread in the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced in the margin of the foundation inside, then extract the thread of that which is pierced, as if you put your knee or foundation; and treat the head of the thread, and assemble the two heads together, and restrain one to the other, and leave it for a day or two; and restrain it at no time, until the threads heal those chars that are between two, and stick together; then cure the wound as long as it is soldered and healed.  
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if it is not too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because it is not fitting to make a wound covering too deeply embedded, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spine which one makes a fistula is very thick on one side and trenching; and on the other side no, for because you do not cut what you do not need to cut, as you see here. 
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhages are according to II manners: or they are within the foundation, as a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in short, they contain blood, and there are one or more, and they are outside the foundation and at the head of the foundation; but those which are outside have little moisture, and even though one or two drops of citrine water or a drop of blood, and they have the color of the body; and the cure of those who have them inside the foundation is that you command the patient to lie down in chambers, as long as the foundations leave him, and the threads appear; then hurry, and you can take them with tweezers, or you hold them with your finger, then cut them at their roots; and if the tweezers cannot hold them because of their moistures, then take them with a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamois; and extract them with your fingers, then cut them, and powder them with some hot powders that be in place of cautery; or you cauterize them as it is said or chapter of cautery, then cure the other cures until it is healed; and if the foundations cannot leave, then administer a clyster to the patient, harsh and biting to wash out what is in the foundation, so that it can come out openly; when the patient gets up, and if the threads are outside the foundation, then the cure is light; and it is that you take them with your finger or tweezers, and cut them, then cure them as we have said, until it is healed, and that he fears the incision by iron. 
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you administer the suture according to this manner: take I thread twisted and put it in a needle, then pull the thread upward and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle and so be wide; and tighten the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do likewise with all the others, and leave one for correcting the superfluity of blood; then put upon the foundation I cloth moistened in rose oil or in cerote, and put on the foundation, and command the patient that he rest; and then leave him as long as it drips, and when they will be dry, then cure with ointment and other cure, until it is healed. 
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of drying of the veins or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying of veins in the intestine, and by constriction of nature, and when the sickness is old and the medicine is no use.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you scrape at the point of a spatula or with your fingernail the bark above, which does not leave it moist; then treat it as long as it heals as it should; and if it cannot heal, then begin scraping again more strongly than before, until it heals well and is scraped; then treat it as long as it is healed.  
dou fremit	about trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants is a small appearance false before the body, and goes much in deep; and sometimes it finds it cold, and feels it as well like death of trembling, and comes in all the body, and more to the hands than other place. 
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a stick from an ostrich feather, or a strong vulture feather, and place that stick on the boil, until the purple circles surround the boil all around; then turn your hand over the entire stick until you cut all around the boil, and put it in the center, and scrape the boil of its roots. 
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see it, so do this of a chain of iron or steel according to this form, and be subtle below and trailing above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	nor pierce it, for to keep the two together, and move pressed And if you see it, so cauterize the furrow, as it is before or chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never is a clyster made of silver or lead, or molten iron or mesh; and never are these instruments small and large, according to those who are administered them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those therefore who are administered in the cure of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clyster is small and large if it is above wide, or the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And there is a rupture where the belly is tied, as you see, and the shoulder blade is pierced inside; and on one side II pierced, and on the other I; and the belly where medicines are put in an animal bladder or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes, and between each hole I must be spaced, then put into these holes I thread of strong thread, twisted in X or whatever around, and assemble the belly as it is a sheepskin; and when the medicine is inside, there is a string at the instrument before a strong thread, then enema; and this is the form of the circle.  
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the chief with clyster of oil or of yolk of egg, or of a similar thing, then put it in gently; then the ministers squeeze its two hands together, until it is all visible, then take out the clyster, and raise the patient's legs to the side, and if the medicine wants to issue, then hold it as much as he can; and if he sleeps a whole night on his stomach, then there is more help.  
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cleanse him with a clyster for a disease of the stomach, and the medicine hastens to work well, so let him restart it until he is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the foundation, or an abscess, then the enema should be as subtle as for a child; and this is the shape of the subtle enema on which the skin is strained: 
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the cure of wounds; or we will say the cures of hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.
