The things by which wounds are made are by blows of stone, and sword and knife, or lance or staff or arrow, or similar things; which are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or chest, or belly, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with wounds of the head simple, because remembrance will come in its chapter. 
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or chief, and the bone is not broken, if take care that it is of gitement of stone or similar things, and the skin is quickly ruptured and the wound is large, and you doubt vehemently an abscess hot: then do so immediately to bleed from the cephalic same as if it comes little blood from the wound, and be the bleeding on the contrary of the part navy; and avoid the patient repletion of wine and thick meats. 
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to bleed, then let him lessen his meat, and drink no wine, nor eat any flesh; and put on the wound, if an abscess comes there, cotton moistened in rose oil alone, or in styptic wine; and if there is no abscess, he puts on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it has not been moved by the air, powder, which I will say a little later; and if he has moved it with fire, put on some ointments, until it is healed.  
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be joined together by tents, then join them with sutures, as I will say for wounds of the belly, of the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is open to the bone, and hangs, and holds only by a piece, then cut it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat large meats, such as beef and cooked wheat, also beans, and similar things. 
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find a skin rottenness and it does not reach the bone, so cut the rot completely, and throw it away, then cure; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by medicine, so seize the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it. 
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and that you put into them this powder which unites as soon as the arsenic has worked.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and grind the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and hold it firmly, until it dries well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it well, and leave it untied, if it does not swell; for do not remove the medicine until it is healed.  
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at no time is this made with only quicklime, when one does not have the frankincense nor the dragon's blood, but that the heat has cauterized the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is moved by fire, even though it is in this state, do not put on this powder; but put some softened ointment, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, as long as it is wet; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.  
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then you shall extract it with subtle pincers; and I will tell you hereafter about the fractures of the head. 
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound comes from the neck and it is simple, if it has no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, there is no other thing to leave the cure, and do not put anything restraining, because it harms the nerve and makes them retreat; and do not put on the wound anything cold, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of them is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, such as wormwood washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and wormwood also washed in sweet water, and other stones of mine according to this manner, and moist ointments.  
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, so sew it and bind it with bandages, then tend to it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is broken and full of bone, pierce or lower there; and if the artery is cut, and bleeding comes, then cauterize it, and apply a bandage, and do what is necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the conduit is kept, by which the meat goes, then sew the heart above the chain of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural figure; and then bind it tightly and leave it for some days, then cure with medicinal ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then set it; and if there are pieces of bone, then treat them outwards as much as you can, and those that you cannot have, then leave them as long as the wound weeps, and be freed and aligned with the exit; and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I have said. 
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and it has a fistula, then treat it as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or a knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or sword, and the wound is deep, look if from the wound there come air bubbles as the patient breathes: then know that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put any powder in at first hour, nor bind it so that the blood does not drain out, and return to the heart, and kill the patient; but put attractive ointment on it, and tie it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound so that it sucks out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for 3 days, or 4, or more; so that there comes no spasm, nor tremor of heart nor strangling of air; and when you see good dispositions, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure therefore with tents and other dressings, as long as it is healing; and if it cannot heal, and work, then know that there is a fistula; so treat the wound as one should. 
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or worse, or on the back, then the cure of those in front; if it is large, with stitching; and if it is small, with powder; and if it is deep into bone, and has broken pieces, then close the wound, and the foreign objects outside if they are loose; and if they are not loose, then let the wound rot, so that it will lighten the extractions; and for other wounds in other limbs, judgment as we have said. 
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the stomach's displacement
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is great and medium and small; from a large wound sometimes the intestine or nerve of the intestines comes out, which introduces worms; and the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes it is worse than a small wound, because one puts the intestines back in with difficulty, if they do not put them back quickly; because the intestine inflates as soon as it feels cold, so they go back in with difficulty, and for this reason the average wound is worse, because one repositions the intestine to its place like the others II And know that the rupture of the belly is according to IIII manners: the II common stitches happen in the stitching of the belly, and the stitching of the other wounds of the body and II other stitches are proper and happen to the other wounds; and all the same they are more proper with the stitching of the belly, and I will say one by one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestines has come out, and it is hard to close, it is done in one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to the cold.  
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth in hot water only, or you cook in hot water with squill and cypress and spice, and moisten the intestine as long as the inflammation is removed; and sometimes make this wine restraining, and it is moved that awe sole for deflating. 
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or wine that they are cooked well, for by this is aligned the entrance a little; and if it cannot enter, make a hole in the wound with the instrument of which one cuts hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to move that tail, that none should cut it unless there be great necessity; and this is the instrument to split it: thus trench within in the curve and outside no, and see here the form. 
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine has jumped out, put it back in according to its natural form in its proper place, if you are able, because it is important for healing.  
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide, and it is in the part below the belly, it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the part below the belly, put the head and buttocks higher than the parts below, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, put your attention to what the injured part is higher than the other; and thus it is necessary to administer what I say in large and medium wounds. 
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	Little wounds put what appears to you, then have between your hands I minister pity that holds all the rupture in his hand, and assemble the lips; and this is the common manner of sutures, and it is that you prick an needle or more, according to the quantity of the breadth of the wound, then leave from the chief of the wound I distance, and there put a needle where it has I good strong thread; and pierce the II heads of the skin with the II heads of the siphac, which is under the skin inside, as long as you make it pierce from that part, and assemble the II chiefs of the siphac the IV together; then the strain of a double thread around the needle of II parts, then assemble the II heads of the wound evenly, and then leave I distance, and there put another needle; then tie the end of the thread as you have done the first needle, and do not cease to do this according to what you need needles, until the whole wound is restrained; and let the needles be medium, between subtle and thick, because the subtle needles cut all the flesh, and the too thick ones cannot enter well: for this reason they must be medium; and it does not become well to put the needles too far out of the flesh and skin, lest they cut and open the wound before the suture; and then cut the heads of the needles so that they do not prick the patient when sleeping, and I put tents or cloths on the heads of the needles for them to keep still, and let them be until the wound is closed; and this manner of suturing with needles is more convenient in small wounds, because it suffices one needle or II Li second suture if it is common, and it is that you assemble the II heads of the skin and the II heads of the syfac together with a needle where there is I medium strong thread; and when you will have pierced these heads all IV together, then return the needle to the part where you began, in the manner in which one sews the robes; and put distance between each suture the thickness of a minor finger; this suture serves man, and I sewed a wound with a man's belly, which was cut by a knife, and it was the wound more than a palm wide, and it had intestines well II palms wide, and the wound was in the middle of the belly. 
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been out for 24 hours, and the wound was healed for 15 days, and I cured him, and he was healthy.  
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the mire had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointment, because I was in the place where one did not find any, nor any medicines; and I put cotton on top of the wound twice a day, and I washed it with honey water until it was healed. 
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the II proper ways of sewing: take the needle, and put it from the outside part to the inside; when it has pierced the core right through, lay the tip down on the skin where you have inserted the needle, and make it pierce from the other side from the inside to the outside; and the understanding of this stitching is that you sew as the furrier does furs, and that you leave one time the thread on one side, and take it on the other, until the stitch is completely done.  
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of suturing, which the Gauls call properly, is like any font, which assembles the two parts together naturally, and applies one end of the suture to the other end, in this manner: pierce an needle or the end of the thread near, and make it pass through that place only, and leave the two ends of the suture; then turn the needle, and make it pass from the outer part to the inner, at the two ends of the suture; then pierce one and the other from the outer part to the inner, at two other threads of the needle that are on the other side; and this is the best manner of suturing and the most common.  
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galens says this word, and no one testifies to it, one must sew the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each; and one must push one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew ropes; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the suture is more serious than the others places of the belly. 
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are like the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh in all its blood, as long as the artery has been moved, so put back the intestine, and the outside; then put on powder with ointment, and if the artery has been moved, put on any ointment that is present, as long as the wound bleeds; and stitch the skin, and be joined the face, and the mirach; then cure the wound like the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, so put on, as soon as it begins to close, old cotton, and move it II times a day until it is healed. 
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	Because you do not need other medicine in multiple arrangements as long as the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not make community with the principal members, it is necessary that you moisten the linen lightly with oil of tempered heat, or with rose oil, and put it around the armpits, and below the buttocks; and if it feels pain or rot in the belly, and many times happens, then give enemas of black wine, and even if the rot comes to the intestine; and pierce it inside, and know that when this is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small. 
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called «jeun» cannot heal when it is pierced, and this is because of the placement of the veins that are in it, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.  
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the bone jumps from the wound, put it back as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become brown or black, then you must tie the place that is black, so that bleeding does not come from it, because there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the ligature, and put the two heads hanging from the part below the wound up to the outside to align the extraction when the bone falls, and the wound bows.  
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, one can restore it in some men, because I have seen that a man was pierced in the belly by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it festered and became a fistula, and from this there were excrement and wind; I put a cure according to what I could, and did not cease to treat it until it was healed, and the edges soldered. 
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sewn, I doubted that the patient had poorly in his belly; and there was no bad, but remained in better dispositions, and eating and drinking; and said any experimenters that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in such manner: take fresh thread with large heads, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the thread has covered the mouth, put it on the two lips so that it strains its mouth up; and then cut the head, and this holds itself so that it cannot untie, then put the other thread after in the same manner as before, until the wound is all closed; and stitch the wound. 
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	That chief if it is burned in the intestine and no nuisance comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestine of a fine thread which is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the head of this thread of intestine that be much cleansed, and then tie to the head of this thread I thread of flax subtle twisted, then put the thread in the needle and sew the intestine, and wind it in the rupture; and this manner of suture of threads is not worse than according to the way of hope and promise; and if the wound is great and wide, even when it is in one of the grails intestines, there is nothing else nor sanctification, except subtlety. 
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it opens, is universally called "fistula," and even when it is closed and bowed inward. 
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the truth a knotted thing hard and white, where one feels no pain, and it is also raised like the feather of a bird; and sometimes in clear bowe, and other times thick; sometimes pointed, and other times enough; and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is nothing but by one of the IX causes: that is to say, by the smallness of blood or flesh; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the lips, that does not let flesh grow; or because there is too much bowe; or the pus is bad, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is a manner of pestilence; or because the property in the region is slow digestion, and slow healing, and swollen by nature; or there are veins or bones; and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Therefore it behooves me to make you know the treatment of fistula which is done by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas happen in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the syphons, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and so on that comes to the property of the principal member, and to similar ones. 
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of grievous healing, and there is only labor, and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to where I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you want to know it, then take a tent of iron or of lead, if the fistula is straight, so if it is crooked; and if the fistula is twisted, so surround it with a subtle tent of lead, because the lead bends easily around the tortuosity; and if the fistula has holes and you cannot well surround it with tents, then clistirize it through one of the holes, because the moisture spreads from one hole to another, and it cleanses it; then surround it wisely as best you can, that you know if there are bones or nerves, and if it is pierced by them, and ask well the patient of the pain that he feels at the pressure of your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you will know truly the place where it is, and if it is far from the joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have said, and remove the fault and the corrupted flesh that are inside; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is well deep of right place, so it is necessary that you cut deep as much as you can, then put tents moistened in an acrid medicine, and place them to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that is remained at the bottom; and then put ointments cleansing healthy flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, so cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, so cut it. 
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not strike the principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then cure the king as long as the corruption is completely removed, then cure the fleshly things until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and returns bent as before, know that you are not gone to the bottom: if uncover and go as far as you can, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is so healed, it is well. 
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this is so, know that corruption is too far along, that you cannot succeed there; if there is nothing else to do but leave it to nature; and if there is a little bone corrupted, and you can draw it with pliers, if you extract it with the instrument suitable for that, and if there are many bones, then draw them all together, leaving none; and if moisture makes you opposite, and there is no error or fear, cut and moisten and flesh, and deliver the bones. 
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, put on the wound something hindering rot, and let it be until the flesh is rotten around the bones, then they will have more easily the bones; and if it's a large bone, like of leg or thigh, so keep only the corruption as long as the blackness is entirely removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a great part of the corruption, and comes up to the marrow of the bone; then it must be cared for and covered all up to the corruption, and then cure it until it is united; and I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example from it and help in your work.  
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man about thirty years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so that the materials came to the leg, and it became inflamed with a large abscess, and there was no external cause to open; but the healers by their folly opened it so much that the abscess opened, and they corroded a lot of material, and it became a fistula, and there came a lot of holes that all festered and moist from the body; and many healers treated him for about two years, and there was no wise man in the art of hands, until I was called to him, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and what flowed through the holes a great deal; and the flesh of the young man became red, and had a yellowish color. 
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I put a tent in one of these holes, and then I searched all the holes, and I found that some came against each other from all parts of the leg. 
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then proceeded, and dug into one of the openings until I discovered a portion of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption came up to the inner bone; I was assured by what appeared to me of the corrupted bone, and thought that there was no other corruption except that which I removed; and I began to restore the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, but could not suture it; and then I started again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I removed it, and then tried to suture the place; but I could only dig around a palm of the bone, and the trace went all the way through its entirety, then I restored it with medicines; and it became healthy and healed quickly, and did not need to start again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and for the fear of death that I had for him. 
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For by the evacuation of blood he often became quite healthy, and in the place of the bone there grew hard flesh, and he was in good health and had no trouble or discomfort at all, neither going nor coming. 
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this manner: take a linen strip and tie it to the head of the bone that opens, and command someone to extend it upwards; and put another linen strip thicker than the first one, and tie it above the flesh that is below the bone, and stretch the head so that you draw the corrupted flesh downward, and uncover the flesh in the place where you want to be, so that the bone does not pierce the flesh; and put a splint or a board below the bone to help cover the corrupted flesh; and it should be treated as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and treated again other times. 
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover all the flesh; then put a stick underneath, and then with the one side to the other side the corruption, and let the thread be long as the length of the corruption; I say as we have said. And if the corruption is at the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and thread the bone where it contains on the other side. And if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is nothing else to do than to cut. And if the corruption is in the thumb of the hand, or in the thumb of the foot, then this thing is very strong, but nonetheless you must inquire about this corrosion, how it opens for you; and purify it in all the ways that you can, but that the vein or the nerve do not make you contrary. And know that there are many incisions and threads to cut these bones, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of them, and their thickness and their delicacy, and their size and their smallness, and their hardness; and for this reason it is necessary to equip each semblance of work with its instrument. And know that the work will show you the instrument that you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of the diseases; so consider the instrument that you need according to what is fitting. 
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder can be harmed by things inside or outside; and when you have medicine for that corruption through the care of medicines, and they do not benefit, then it is necessary to cover that member up to the place where the corruption comes from so that the patient escapes through this death, or through the malice, which is greater, of the defect of the limb; and the signs are that the member becomes black, so that it seems as if it were burned by fire, and bristles after the blackness, then goes that corrosion of the member to member, and takes over the whole body; so haste to cover, and if it is from the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as a scorpion of the sea and viper and similar ones, if the corrosion is at the head of the thigh, cover it, and do not give him any space to come to the hand.   
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, cut at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, cut at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no other treatment except the quantity of its virtue; and do this in all cases when the corrosion comes or foot: if it comes to the first joint, cut after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, cut the whole foot; and if it mounts to the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other way but to leave the patient to death; and the manner of cutting or sewing the limb is that you tie it above and below, and extend one minister on one of the ligaments down, and another minister on the other ligament up, and you dissect the flesh which is between the two ligaments a spatula wide, so that the bone is uncovered; then cut or sew, and put a linen cloth on each side, so that the suture does not touch the healthy place, and comes to the patient another lesion and abscess. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you work, cauterize the place carefully, or put on some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the limb wrapped in a good bandage, and cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his foot: he had a blackness that seemed burned by fire, and this corrosion first came in his heel of the foot, until it engulfed the entire foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cover his foot, and was healed; and long after, the corrosion returned to him in his hand, and he came to me, and I put on him things that are helpful after the purification of the body, and could not stop the corrosions; and he said to me that I should cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of healing the matter; and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would die, because the strength of the man was weak; and he despaired altogether, and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and was healed; and I have recounted this story only for this reason, that when you need it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess comes in a fleshy place, and stays so long that it makes a great collection of pus; then it bursts and breaks open, and the pus flows out, as well as vessels; and the skin which is above is also as thin as linen cloth, and does not reach to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a disease is called "boil" and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so elongated that it comes to the bone even through, then it is called "fistula"; and the skin is that you cut the whole skin around it, and even when it is thin, as well as linen cloth; and does not heal because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have faith that the skin has hardened, and the corruption is not yet complete, and the skin is thick with flesh, so treat with a clyster like this: see if the breast is large, and the bow which is in it is of foul odor, then cleanse with Egyptian medicine, which is made thus: take ashes, oil, and litharge, equally, and put the concoction into a vessel over the fire, until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey; and then take some according to your need, and mix it with water and honey, and clysterize the breast, and restrain the anus; and leave the medicine inside for two hours, then remove it by squeezing; do this many times, until the breast is purified, and the foulness is gone; and sometimes clysterize with water of ashes, when this medicine is not present, and that you take ashes of vine wood, and pour water over them, then strain it, and clysterize, as long as you know that the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot bear the Egyptian medicine or the water of ashes, then clysterize with water and honey, or with a little ground litharge mixed in; or you can clysterize with honey and warmed wine, because honey has the property of purifying and washing, and the wine dries up the flesh; and when you have done this, and you are certain that the breast is well purified, then clysterize with what makes flesh grow in it, and that is: take diaphana plaster, and mix it with rose oil and wine; or you can clysterize with some other medicines and ointments, about which I have spoken in the treatment of ointments; and if the wound of the breast is small, and the nozzle of the clyster cannot enter, then enlarge it with a iron bit, and put inside a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basil ointment, until it is enlarged; and if the wound is too wide, sew it up so that only the place where the clyster can enter remains open, and if the pus from the breast is on top, then cut or lower the area where it is. 
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bow is in place, do not let anything be put on it; and if you cannot cover the wound as you want, then arrange it in such a way that the bow goes to the lowest point that there is, for when the bow is in place, do not let anything be put on it, and if you cannot cover the wound as you want, then arrange it in such a way: that the bow goes lightly down, and do not leave anything of the bow; and take medicines that consolidate to put on the wound, and stay on top of the linen cloth that covers the whole wound; then cut forcefully at the opening of the chest a little wider than the first, then put ointment under the other cloth according to the quantity of the opening, and put it on the wound so as to align the bow, and do not remove the large cloth outside except after many days once; and the one that is on the opening of the chest, often removes to take out the bow, and know what runs from the bow, if it is venom or a little or enough, or digested, or indigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when the medicine has spread in this way, and you see nature that jumps on the wound, then know that the chest heals already, and approaches health; and then untie it in the morning, or the third day, and when you untie the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the chest lies bowed ingestible after many days, know that the chest does not heal well.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons are cut after a long time, if it does not make you despair of health, for health approaches. 
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men who late healing of flesh in their wounds, and of those who do the opposite; and if a bow is indigested jumps from the chest after many days, know that the breasts don't heal well; and if the breasts take long to heal, and are far apart, then adjust medicines drying moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as ointment diaphinit, for there is great part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine; take ointment diafinit, and do it with rose oil, and the rose of old wine equal in substance; then confit it and use it; and the same made honey cooked engroissment, when ointment diafinit is not present, or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind it, and powder on the honey when it is on the fire; and then glue I drape it, and put it on the chest, and at times administer one long aristologe, and roots of celestial lily, which is also as flour of vetiver and centaury; and use of simple or of compounded: grind them, and make powder, and put on the honey that I have said, and use; and if the cure is lengthened, and is not cured by this cure, then know that corruption is in depth, and makes impression on the bone, or on hard members, or on limbs; so the cure of fistule, as we have said before. 
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the angle
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises under the fingernail of the hand, or the foot, or by chance arises in other places; and when it is neglected, and one does not take care of it, then it comes to a swollen abscess, and runs and throws pus until it runs to the root of the finger, and perhaps all of it; and come the corrosions up to the bone, so much that there comes a putrid pain, and is the limb of the two large, and is the color flux. 
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut to it iron all the superfluity that is left from the wound, then cauterize the wound afterward. 
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauteries is a great help if the bone is healthy, and the fingernail is healthy; and if the nail presses on the flesh, and it begins to prick, and to turn blue, then it is necessary that you put the root under the nail so that the flesh does not rise, and throw it upwards, and cut that flesh subtly and lightly, and put on the rest of the flesh medicines burning and corrosive in order to remove all; then cure with ointments until it is healed. 
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it and treat it carefully, for as long as the bone is corrupt it cannot heal; and if you see that the bone will become corrupt, then cut it in one of us as it was said before, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is broken and pushed, and he feels great pain, then you must first heal it. Then cut the angle of the spatula sharply by cutting sideways above, and guard so that the cut does not come to the flesh which is below the angle, because the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, put something on top that soothes. 
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the sore does from the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints that are born in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is some where there are bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, where the birth is in some of us the thumbs. 
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born in any joint of the thigh does not move, and he who is born at the joint of the thigh, by chance moves; the size of the one who is fleshy is light, in such a manner: cut it at its root with a wide spatula.  
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born in the root of the joint, is grievous to cure; so keep it from being cut.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or should be at the rear end, it is necessary that you cut first the fleshy roundness until the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable thread for this, then cure it until it is healed.  
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The seams that come to two together come by birth, or by soldering of a wound, or by burning of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If it is necessary that you tie this suture so that the parts repay according to their natural forms; then put between two tents or cloths softened in rose oil, so that they do not stick together; or you put between two pieces of thin wood, until the bones are fused, as is necessary. 
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If soldering comes to none of its two with the palm, then that soldering as it is fitting.
des vils	of the bad 
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large swollen vessels full of melancholic excesses, which come in more members of the body; and more happen in the legs of those who go on foot and who work and carry, than to others.  
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore it is necessary that you administer to him once purging of colocynth, and then the herb from the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron is done in two ways: one is to cauterize and draw out the black blood; and the other manner is that you open the vein and drain it entirely.  
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The leg is treated in this manner: first, raise the leg in hot water very forcefully until the large vein becomes soft and pliable, then strain the leg of the patient from above the hip to the area below the knee; then cut the vein in I place, or II, or III, with a broad incision, then lift and pull out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the virtues of the sick person can endure; and then tie it up and order him to remain on meat stewing adding black coal; and recommence the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and hurt the patient. 
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The elevation of the limb is done in this manner: place the leg of the patient, if there is a lot of hair, then put it in water and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell; and if you have no bath, heat it by fire, and then cut above the vein from the top of the knee to the head of the thigh, or in the part below the ankle; then open the skin with the knife, and scrape the vein on each side, until it appears when you feel it; and it is seen red and black, and when it enters the skin it appears like a white cord; then put the root underneath, until it is lifted from the skin, and then put it in the knife lightly, then cut it in another place above three fingers; then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears, then lift it to the raiser, as you did before, and put it on another knife, as you did first; then cut another piece, or more if you need them, then lift it, and cut at the ankle of the foot, then lift and treat it up to the second cut; then strain from one cut to the next, until it comes out completely, then cut it; and if you cannot draw and lift it, put a needle in all the thick double thread, and tie and pull it, and put it under the root, and turn your hand on each side until it comes out; and keep it from cutting, for if it cuts, it cannot be drawn or lifted, and it leads to discomfort for the patient; and when you have treated it completely, put wool soaked in wine and rose oil over the wound site; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the bone is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before. 
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of the iron with which one strikes the vein is curved, and does not cut, so that it does not strike the vein; and it is of thick curve, because if it were thin, it would strike the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and here is the shape: 
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein 
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in hot places where no herbs or trees grow, and in land that has no moisture; and it happens by chance to be born elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens because of the rot that comes under the skin, as it comes from within the body serpents and worms, embedded between the skin and flesh. 
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then it changes its place, and begins the vein to flow out, like a root of a plant.
