Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the head is open, it befits that you envelope around a piece of plank from one and a half to two inches, and the knot, and leave the plank on the leg, and all times that there is point at the end, then enclose around the plank, and the knot; and if it is too long, then cut off a part, and enclose the remaining, and do not cut it in its root, until it is entirely out; for if you cut it, it enters into the flesh, and brings abscesses and rot to that place, and bad disease; therefore for this reason, it befits that it be treated little by little up to the head, and nothing remains on the body; and sometimes this vein when it is treated of five palms of long, or ten, and one man came to me once, whose it was from ten palms of long, and when you cut it, it brings forth the root or through, and pierces it to the bottom, so that all comes out; and be emptied the matter which is inside, and administer to the place medicines preventing rot any day, then cure it like abscesses. 
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes in this vein mains rains, and even when it opens at the joint of the foot, or foot, and there comes much of pus, and from which it jumps rain; cure therefore as we have said before. 
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that are born between skin and flesh 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land “beef disease,” because it happens many times to oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body going up and down, and one feels it well at the edge of limb by limb, as long as it reaches the skin where it goes, and jumps; and is generated from rot of some humors, such as come worms and snakes and lice and roundworms in the belly; and one doubts its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it goes up to the head, and it comes to the eye, by chance enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times. 
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see him being cured and treated, it is not possible for him to go free until he heals; so it is necessary that you bind his place above and below with a strong ligature tightly, then cut above and treat the wound, and if the sting has gone deep into the flesh, and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it corrodes the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or chief near the eye, hold the eyebrow below it firmly, then cut above, and treat the wound; and it is necessary to use the patient with purification of body medicines solutives for the humors stored up, and avoid eating rotten meats. 
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain which comes from windiness 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vakir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in some limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you. 
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and I saw after a little while, it rose as a worm at the shoulder, faster than any thing, like lively silver when it moves from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and went into the shoulder, and then after a little while it spread throughout the whole body, until she came to the other arm; then she told me that she was returning toward the other side of the body, as I saw her. 
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how she moved thus from limb to limb, for I have never seen this illness in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I have wanted many to move pain from their place to another, but I did not want it, as I saw it in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins discovered, and for this reason appeared that constraint of ventositez; and they do not appear according to this reason to those who are delicious, and who have moist bodies and veins covered. 
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to cure this ailment, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said, so lie above and below carefully, and then cut above as much as that windiness is constrained in place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, so cure him who removes the windiness, such as pills fetid, and pills of serapin, and similar others. 
des saiettes	of arrows 
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearance and the places in the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that some have large points, and small, and haired, and smooth; and some which have II angles, and those which have tongues, and those which have pieces; and the one which falls in any member falls according to II manners: or in a principal member as brain, heart, liver, stomach, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members. 
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls therefore in any place of these members, and the sign of death, which I shall tell you after, appear to you: then it behoves you to refrain from the extraction of this arrow, because death comes afterward in many dispositions; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not yet deeply embedded, then treat it, and cure the wound. 
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when an arrow falls and pierces the bone, and leaps the syfac which is above the brain, is when there is scotomy and sode and esvertin and rouge in the eyes, and inflammation and rouge of the tongue, and spasm and permixtion of understanding, and vomiting of mucus; and perhaps it without force from the nostrils, or ears; and perhaps loses the speech and voice; and leaps from the wound moist white seeming to poults, and also leaps as burning of flesh; and if this sign appears to you, then hold yourself from the cure, and treat the arrow if it is not inside. 
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the seventh when it falls or core, is that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were tied in a hard thing, not empty; and perchance the seventh moves also like the hand, and comes out black blood, and coldness and cold sweat, and syncope: know then without doubt that death will come. 
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the little arrow that does not come out is that without pains of foam leaps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, and sighs loudly and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the shoulder, it is near the ribs; and it gives great pain and great suffering and sighing; and it moves all the members from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls into the stomach, perhaps some undigested food will jump out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly, and nothing of straw comes out through the intestines, there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine comes out with it and flows, and the patient feels intense pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the arms and necks and throat and shoulder and auxiliary and spine of the back and  forearms and hips and legs, and similar members, are saved according to more dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, for this reason that you do something like that.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to the man with an arrow that stuck in the root of his nose: I pulled it out and dragged it from the other side under the fat of the ear, and it was healed without pain at all. 
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And in a game an arrow was shot that fell into the grease of the oil under the paper, and the arrow was retrieved, and it could not be reached except for the point towards the shaft, and the arrow was large as a Turkish bow, at all light iron without ears; the game was safe, and no bad accidents happened to him.  
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And treat an arrow in the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I removed the barbs, and carefully extracted it as long as I did, and the Christian was healed. 
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And treat an arrow in a man, that it was in the chest or belly, and thought that he would die; and then when he had passed XXX days, he did not change his disposition; I cut above the arrow, and tightened it, and pulled it out, and there were no bad accidents. 
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if a man has an arrow in his back or hip, and the wound was sewn up; and the arrow remains inside, and does not change its natural positions, nor finds inconvenience in any of its natural works. 
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And look at another man, to whom an arrow fell in his face, and the wound was sutured; and he remained so suffering great pain; and many others like it. 
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And treated an arrow in the man of princes the king, that it was lodged between his ribs, and was a little inclining to the right part; and the arrow was entirely set, I was called to the cure after that it was struck three days. 
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very narrow. 
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I felt it with a very fine probe, and did not feel anything; and he felt pricking and pain below his right ear. 
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought that it was from the point of the arrow I put on its place a poultice atractive and digestive, because the leg did not swell; and there appeared to me the legs of the arrow. 
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the plaster on the wound for several days, and closed the wound directly, and kept the patient there for a long time, until he felt the arrowhead one day inside his body; and he told me this.  
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put on the wound medicine sharp and corrosive for many days, until it was open, and I touched it, and felt the head of the arrow which was hardening in place; then I adjusted it in the opening of the wound with that medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me; and it progressed well the ends during IIII months, and then enlarged so much the wound that I put in tweezers, and mine on one side and the other, and could not exit; therefore I did not cease to subtilize and to devise ways of instruments, until I took I day the tweezers well made, according to those which its form will come at the end of this chapter, until I pulled it out, and restored the wound. 
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the wise men judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I restored it then, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was healed completely. 
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you apply your care to those that I do not say, for the books cannot comprehend all; but the wise masters compare on well small things, and on those that are present and lacking, find new work, and new instruments, in the understanding of strange things that happen in this art. 
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows are not from the members where they are fixed except according to II manners: or by the place where they enter, or by another part; and that which is by the place where it enters, it is an arrow entering in its flesh, and that which is no longer now. 
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not jump now, leave it so long as the bone is carried around, and let the issue be healed; and also if it is fixed in the bone, and it cannot come out, leave it thus for several days, and move it every day; and then it jumps, and if it does not jump, pierce around to all I forest fine, until the hole around is enlarged, and then treat it.  
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head, and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient: then do not remove it, but leave it until it is equal after some days, because if the arrow comes to this place, it is death. 
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is lodged only in the bone and does not come to the surface, and the patient remains for some days without bad accident, if the engine of the treatment.  
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply stuck and cannot be drawn out further, then administer the aforementioned poultice, as I have told you; then cure the place until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is put back in its place in the body, if one cannot see it, search all around it; and if you feel it, then treat it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot by the narrowing of the wound, and by the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones or nerves or vein, then widen as much as the wound is large; and treat the arrow if you can, and if it has ears at what it holds, then remove the flesh that is stuck from both parts to where you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, as much as you can draw it out; and be careful that you do not break the arrow, that you draw it out more grievously. 
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, then put it back into its place until the pain is reduced, then treat it, because the extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood makes you go against it, administer what we have said of the cure in its chapter; and guard yourself from incision of the nerve and the vein, and put engine as well as you can move to draw out the arrow without peril, whether soon or late, or firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form that it was when the arrow fell into it, for that is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot, then put it according to what the signs show you. 
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where one sees or feels nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in place if it can be seen or felt: cut therefore above, as long as the pliers can take hold, and then extract it: if it jumps out now. 
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be drawn out, leave it there for now, and then restart the extraction until it comes out; and if it is of the arrow, take the entire shaft; and if the shaft has fallen, and you see to administer thrusting, then administer the tool with a pointed end so that the tip of the arrow enters into the point of the instrument; and then thrust, and if the arrow is lodged, put the instrument back in with the point entering again, in order to facilitate extraction. 
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is surrounded, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then cure the wound as is proper. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls or in the belly or at the bladder or at the ribs, and it is close, and you can cover it up, then it shall be covered. And guard yourself from covering the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then stitch the wound, if it is necessary; and care for it until it is healed. 
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows are similar to the beak of an eye, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The form of the tip of the bolt is like the feather of a bird, to insert at the point of the arrow, as this is its form. 
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of pliers to put in and to know if it is here:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins from which one is healed, of which there are XVI in the head, that is to say: II veins which are behind the ears, which are called the two "herbech"; and the II arteries which are in II temples appearing; and II veins that are in II tear ducts of II eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the neck; and the II veins that are on the throat; and the II veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and II veins that are under the tongue. 
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins which are commonly used in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side of the ribs, and the common people call it “vein of the head”; and the middle one is called “fast”, and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilica, and the common people call it “vein of the heart”; and the basilica is on the right side of the ribs, and the common people call it “vein of the belly”, and it is above the fossa, and it is the one that we use to draw blood which opens clearly above the pouch.  
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saphenous vein is the one that is between the ring finger and the little finger, and there are two of them; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: the one is below the curve of the pocket on the left side, and the second saphenous which is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein that is called “saphenous,” which is in the ankle on the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below those. 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bloodletting of the veins that are behind the ears so helps with old catarrhs, and with migraine; and the qualities of the vein, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a vise, until the two veins appear behind the ears in their dependence on the head: then aim at your right side, and where you feel the pulse below your hip, so rule it; then take the lancet, and put it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand over the entire vein above, and cut and the skin and the vein well the two points of the passage, and make blood flow as much as you see; then strain and tie it, until it is healed; and I have already said the incision and cautery in the first book. 
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bloodletting of the II arteries that are in the II temples, it is good for migraine old, and sudden, and habitual ophthalmia, and to the body of tears sharp at the eyes; and the qualities of the bleeding are as I say: and is that the patient restrains his neck, until the II veins appear openly; and feel the pulse below your right side, and then point down; then lift the heart above the vein on your right index, and put the lancet under, and lift the vein up, and the cut, as you have done in other veins, and do correction of blood according to your need; then untie the patient, and put your right hand on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton; and then the scab forms, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken about them and their cutting and their extraction, or the beginning of the book. 
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bloodletting of the vein in the forehead is as valuable as the bloodletting of the cephalic vein for diseases of the face, and for migraine, and for gout. And its qualities are that the patient restricts his neck by twisting it until the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", whose form is: 
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point on the vein, and hold firm with your hand, or another thing, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see; then bind the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is healed and never again open it with a wide flame. 
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not proper that the flames be too thick; and heal across because the bone is close, and perhaps break the flames when they are subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood of the two veins that are in the two tear ducts helps the eyes, and to the cheek, and to the temple, and to the corner of the eye, and to the ailments of the face; and the qualities of their blood are that the patient strains his neck by twisting with any linen, as before; then the vein is drained, and whether the vein is through a short, long, or wide flame, because there is no flesh. 
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, perhaps it breaks; then make a correction with blood, as much as you need, and then tie it on cloth, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood of the vein of the nose is good for fever, and for sore throat, and for diseases of the face, like migraine and redness that comes in the face, even when it is old. And the qualities of the blood are that the patient tightens his collar, then he strains his nose to your left hand, and takes the fine long flame, and puts it between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well until now, and the sinews begin to correct; and do not go too deep, and make a correction of blood according to your need, then bind it at night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame: 
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the II veins helps in the treatment of  the armpit, and in the beginning of measles, and many diseases, and pestilence, and corrosion, and herpes, and smallpox; and the qualities of the blood are that the patient strains his neck under both sides, as we have said; and let the master be standing above the head of the sick person, and the sick person sitting on the seat, then open the vein in a long one a little widely, then draw out blood moderately, or as much as is necessary; then redo another part in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and tighten the veins moderately, so that the patient does not strangle; and leave him until morning, that the wound may be healed.  
de la sainie des leivres	of the veins of the books 
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bloodletting of veins of the lips above helps in the ulcer in the mouth, and the corruption of gums, and fissures of lips, and sores and ulcers.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of the vein are to make the patient sit before you, and restrain his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one is on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by those that are black, and by those that around them have small black veins: cut therefore both, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, cut the largest of each side, and just as well the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner. 
de la sainie desoz la lengue	from the vein under the tongue 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The vein of the veins that are below the tongue so help after the bloodletting of the cephalic, and it is to the constriction of the throat, and to the diseases of the eye, and to the diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of the bleeding is that the patient lies between your hands in front of the sun, and he lifts the tongue, and look below on each side a vein black: bleed then one and the other, and do not go too far into them, for under there are the arteries. 
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the cut, which are commonly opened in two ways: either pricking with a sharp instrument all along the vein's course; or with a subtle olive as trenchant knives, and it is called "anvil"; and they are wide and fine according to the width and depth of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirror is very renowned, and is as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And there is need to open the veins that are full of gross blood apparent, and that contain thick and troubled blood; and this is the form of the olive flame:  
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle pointed, and is for healing veins subtly, where there is subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are below the throat, and at the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly; and it befits the patient to bleed wisely, and that he should avoid the artery which is below. 
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he feels the ground, and blood flows out, then it should be stanched as I have said; and the flame should not prick but cut like a knife. 
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, then it behooves you to constrain it, and change another; or you desire no vein of it, or you heal in its place the vein removed from the arm: it opens manifestly; and the cup at the flame is healed, as we have said. 
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see to know the place of the vein, then it is fitting that you extract the arm, that you touch the place as much as you know the pulse; then sign the place with a fire brand, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein of the flaming needle; and guard that you do not wound in the artery when you see the place inflamed, for it is from the artery: escape therefore. 
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it rise up like the urine of a child, and the vein is red and thin, know that it is blood from an artery: haste yourself therefore, and put your hand above lengthwise, then remove your hand if the vein is still, as often happens; bind his arm, and leave him so, and do not move him, the patient; and be without fear, and do not move him until he is healed. 
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if his arm is not set straight, and he feels pain, and the medicine is not present, then tie off the artery if it opens up, because the head of the retraction; and set the arm straight.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a strip of fig bark, and cut it, and take one half and tie it well until the other day; if it does not hurt, that is good; if not, cure it, as we have said, with powders that stop blood; and the stopping is not harmful in more positions for the small wound, and the strength of the band on the arm.  
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein in the middle is helped so that it draws blood from the top of the head and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilica and the cephalic, as we have said; and it behoves the surgeon to place himself toward the nerve which is below, and if he does not pierce too deeply, and finds the nerve, and he swells and the health is grazed, and by chance cannot heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any man because of its subtlety, then it behooves you to feel the vein with the aneth instrument; and touch the nerve with your power. 
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if it has a vein between the two nerves, then make an incision along the length
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The cephalic vein helps to draw blood from the head and helps the eyes; it is necessary to bleed in the olive branch or the myrtle branch, because it is the safest of all veins, for it has no tendon, nerve or artery.  
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to seek the lightest position, and do not worry if it takes the first time, and you begin again; and by chance some men swell the joints at times when one attempts the first time, but it does nothing harm. 
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The qualities of the vein are according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing that you must know about bloodletting, if it is brought only to maintain health, and to avoid diseases to come; and let the blood be drawn in one of the III veins that are or course: namely, cephalic, femoral, and basilica; and it should be done at the beginning of Lent on Monday, and in Autumn and Winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and it should be done the first day or the third, after II hours or III days.  
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bloodletting which is administered to illnesses has no determined hour, but when need is of day or of night, at all hours and in all times; and it does not behoove to bleed children until XIV years, nor woman carrying fruit from the fourth month until the seventh. 
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Do not bleed the old man who has passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when some wants to be bled, in whatever manner that may be, it is fitting that he prepare the intestines with a light enema, if he has much mucus retained, so that the veins do not attract the superfluities of waste harmful to the principal members; nor should one bleed anyone who is too full of meats, nor who is drunk, as long as it is known; nor hydrops; and worse to bleed after colic pain, vomiting, diarrhea, and multiplication of labor in women, and childbirth, watching and fasting, and that which all virtue, or by means of the weapon or of the body; then subtilize the humors, if his blood is thick, by meats and by drinks and by medicines, if you have the power to do so; then go into a bath, if nothing prevents you, to subtilize the blood, and bleed from the vein at the side below the armpit, as we have said; and guard yourself that day from work, from exertion, from lust, and similar things; and be quiet and joyous, and let the one who bleeds be higher than he who is being bled, and rub his arm two or three times, then restrain the thread above the middle, for when it is too loose or tight, it cannot correct the blood; and then rub the place with your hands, until the veins swell, and you feel them; then moisten the one being bled with a drop of old oil, then put his finger from his left hand on that vein below the point where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not become too open and easily pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that are as thick as cords in the groin, and some that are full of windiness, so that when one puts fire to them, they withdraw from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus it is with some; and if one opens the vein, then the wound is too tight, for this reason, therefore, it is necessary that the surgeons be advised in these things.  
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is worked on the first time, it is good; if not, he begins again a little below where it was, if the veins are not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the limb is swollen, and the patient is frightened, let him rest for one or two days, and do not bind up his arm: for fear there will come a boil; nor enter into bath, then begin the discharge if he wishes; and if the puncture is small, or the vein short subtle, and you doubt that it does not contain so much blood as you see, then prick in the same place to the whole flame directly; and work a little, so that the limb be swollen; for this happens many times, when the wound is small. 
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place wounded, do not begin the bloodletting again, and put on a bit of oil, because it closes the body of the blood, and is mixed in this place the oil that the wound; and thus administer the oil in each bleeding that you bleed the veins, to stop the course of blood; and this same thing does trickle and bow of it, when one puts it on the place; so subtly the blood and it parts when it is too large. 
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes an abscess that is large, which happens often, even when it is drained only once and the opening of the vein is small, so hasten, and place on top a sponge moistened in water and salt a little hot, and restrain it for one hour; and it is necessary that you do this after the issue of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place afterwards for several days, without any blackening or greening, then it does not harm him; and if you see, place on top anything of aloes or myrrh put in juice of calament, monstastre, or similar. 
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times abscesses and appearance to the basilica's  health: put therefore your hand on, and if you find the place soft at the pressure of the hand, so is that appearance evil.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid therefore that you put on anything of those we have said, for by chance it may lack the artery; but let him I bandage I plaster dry to harden the place, then its care other care, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each one with blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it ooze until it is red; and if you see it swollen, let it subside until it is smaller; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for the one who is plump and full, and has need of bloodletting, that a larger wound be made, and that the flames be wide; and to the one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed him little by little and often, and he must be bled by cutting crosswise, not by pricking; and this manner of bleeding is safe from loss of blood and cutting of nerves, and is more useful than bleeding long or wide.  
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to one whose body is weak from blood loss, it is necessary to give soft bread in pomegranate juice; if he is hot, treat him with blood three or four times. And if he is of cold complexion, mix soft bread before the wound with mucid syrup, or with aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-smelling syrup. 
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it pulses at the vein, after the exit of much blood, then it behooves him to moisten broth of flesh and fragrant syrup and use the other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope for the opening of veins. 
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to empty his arm, and bleed other times, if it is needed, when he is weakened by much bleeding, that he bleed little by little, according to the quantity of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to empty his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, he bleeds seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to bleed from another part, he must bleed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body that is already hot and causes fever; so it is necessary to draw out a great quantity, and widen the opening as much as it will drip in pieces; then when you have treated all the conditions of health, and put your hand on his arm when he is healthy, that death does not come in place of pieces, and this happens many times, when the healer is negligent; and it is not necessary when you see to loosen his arm, and let blood a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press strongly on it; nor if it is curved, that he extends his arm widely, for that would be bad; but let him rest as much as he is healthy the second time; or you put it to the point of the flame, until the blood which is frozen at the opening of the vein comes out, and put on top a little piece of wool set in water, and press lightly. 
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not constrict it at all, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires drawing blood a second time, let it be done in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is bled in the place of the vein in the neck because it is composed there.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of the vein is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the bone is red; then be bound moderately so that the vein appears well, then drain it now through, neither wide nor long; and let the openings be wide, and drained well near the joint of the hand, and if he cannot pull it out, put the hand back in hot water, and leave the blood there in the water until you have enough; and if it is in summer, do not put the hand back in hot water, because one puts it more in winter than in summer; and the vein of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve.  
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The blood of the vein of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it is done: restrain the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein is swollen, if you can see it; and if the vein is crooked, and if you cut it completely through, it does not grieve anything; and do not go too deep, because the nerves are below all covered with skin, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the blood is congealed in the wound, and cannot issue. 
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is necessary, then put oil and wool on top of the vein to keep it covered tightly, and do this for each one.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sinew of the left hand is good for the disease of the mouse, and do everything as I have told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sap of the sophene is good for all diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the marrow, and retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and hips and old legs, and similar diseases. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of his medicine is that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it throbs, and ties above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there go many veins; so heal where the larger vein, or at the ankle, that is better. 
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cut it above the foot, guard the nerves which are below, and cut in a way similar to when cutting into [something]; and let the flame be annealed.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot flow out, put the foot back in water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the first time the wound fails, recommence the second one above a little, because the place is salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and thus make of the soap from the other foot equally.  
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle of the foot, and its bleeding is good for the pain in the hip, when it is hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the qualities of its vein are that the patient enters into the bath, and strains above the ankle four fingers by twisting it, because otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, then you cleanse it in all the ways that you can, and across; and it is better that you make it open than that you cut it, because the skin is dry, and it is much replenished at men's hands.  
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, see that there is no pain in the one who opens or the back of the foot, and towards the small toe, and guard the nerves; and make as much correction of blood as you see, and then untie the tie, and put on cotton and restrain it; she is now healed. 
des sainies de ventouse	of ventosa wounds 
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leeches are made of horns, or glass, or wood; and leeching is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is felt to hurt so much is according to II manners: or it is with fire, or without fire; and cupping that is done by striking and extracting blood is done in XIIII leus of the body, of which one is all in the head; and the other is in the neck; and II others in II ribs of the neck; and the ventouse below the chin; and the ventouse of II shoulders; and the ventouse above the hips; and the ventouses between II arms; and the ventouses of II legs; and the ventouses of II ankles; and cupping does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason it does not weaken one as much as when one makes bloodletting from a vein; and it is not fitting that it be administered, neither with fire nor without fire, in any illness that comes from repletion, until all the body is emptied. 
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of illness it is necessary to bleed, or by custom, we must bring them each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in every time; for there are such who, when they have need to bleed, have a heavy head; and there are those who feel fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and at the neck, and darkness to their eyes; and some who feel a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and leak blood; and there are those who dream, and see through blood and nightmares and death and similar things. 
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when it is removed after.iii. hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bloodletting of the head helps in the great pain of the head... that comes to the eyes, and it is not fitting that this be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this cupping is in place of the cephalic bloodletting, and it is not fitting for him who is of cold complexion to use it, or who has catarrh, for this does them great discomfort; and for this reason, it is not fitting that the elderly use it, nor those who have or head colds diseases.  
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal from it often become oblivious, and for this reason it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower due to the fear of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The windpipe is in the place of the vein of the head and of the basilica, and for that reason it is good for the treatment of pain, and for the opening of the channel of the throat, and all, and for repletion; and one should not block it too much, because if it is held too firmly, it creates an obstruction in the stomach or heart.  
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The punctures of the II ribs of the neck are worth as much as pains in the head, and in the ophthalmia and migraines, and in the strangling, and to the pain at the roots of the teeth, and is in place of the basilary vein; and it is necessary that you command the healer that he express his hand when putting it on, so that he does not cut the artery, and does not come a hemorrhage. 
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventilations below the chin are good for mouth disease, and gum rot, and similar ailments that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is good for illness that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The bleeding of the veins with a knife is worth as much as three veins of the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the patient not to put too much pressure on them, because their skin is bare of flesh, and lies over nerves and arteries.  
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup which is on the haunches is good for hemorrhoids of the foundation, and for diseases below, and it should be large, and of iron, that it has need to well draw; and perhaps if it were thin, it would break; and in this way it makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups of the legs are applied openly, because they attract blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains of the hips, and of the thighs, and of the bladder, and soften the tumors; and they are placed in the place of the two calves, and of the two ankles, but nonetheless they weaken the body after long use, and bring weakness in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of putting the suction cup is that you put it first empty, and succeed temperately, and place it firmly, and move it equally, and do not cease to do this, until you see the place red and inflamed, and appear the color of blood; then firm, and replace the suction cups, and take care in the disposition of the body, because there are such who have tender flesh, and clear pores: so it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, it is necessary to pierce it twice: the first time to thin the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it is necessary to pierce it a third time; and when we want to draw blood little by little, we only prick once.
