Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want much blood, let us often return to it; and if the vein is strong, then we pierce it well, and the ends are that the veins be pierced soundly, and it is necessary for him who has thick skin and hard, and who have porous pores, that you oil their places with suction cups of appetizing and dissolving oil: If it is in winter, of violet oil, or almond sweet oil, or seed oil of gourd; and if it is in summer, of cress oil, or lily, or chamomile, or similar. 
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is large and cold, then take bitter oil, or balm, or dill seed oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one whom one heals has tender skin and large pores, one should not put any oil on it, but one should wash it after the ventosaion of rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or gourd water, or porcelain water, or something similar. 
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, let them rise from rosemary water, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large superfluities raise themselves from old wine, or from seuc water, or from a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and it is not fitting to bleed with cupping before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath an hour or II; and do not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he lie down when he must be cupped and when he is cupped. 
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And guard those who are recovering are choleric, and if their skin is too much agitated and inflamed; then it befits them to eat cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuce at the meal, and similar things; and suck milk, and meat of roasted pig, and moist meats. 
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, take syrup of honey and fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and mints, and  mince rue and small parsley and sparrows; and the day that he will be bled, he should drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men no times triacle or muscate before or after bleeding, to comfort the main limbs; and let it be subtle the root, but it is not necessary that those who are hot drink it. 
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are placed without hurting are those that are placed on the liver, and on the thigh, and gout, and on the belly and the groin and the hips and the hip joint, because these parts do not suffer to be hurt on their own, and one does it only in order to draw blood from limb to limb, as we put them on the breasts when the child is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we put suction cups on the belly and on the groin to diminish the limb; and to remove the pain, when there is an obstruction or a stone, so it removes by its attractive virtue perhaps the obstruction, or dislodges the stone from its place; and thus it does when one puts it on the liver and on the thigh when there is held-back windiness, and these suction cups are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and some times filled with warm water, as in maladies of pleurisy, and in such a manner one fills the suction cup with hot water alone, or with water in which herbs have been boiled suitable for this. 
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it shall have two sides of a width and half a palm from the forefront, and have or cost on the side near the middle, as for putting a needle, and be of iron, so that it does not blister the patient when placed upon the limb; and have in the middle a crossbar of iron or steel, to put a heated candle into, and they should be both large and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who take them; for the suction cups of children are other than old people, and the thin than the fat. 
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one must thus put this suction cup on the limb:  take the wick of wax or linen, and place it in the suction cup through the hole that is in the suction cup, so that the light is at the bottom of the suction cup so that it does not burn the patient; and then put it on the limb, and the dressings should be on the puncture that we have said, so that when one wants, vapor goes in, and you take off the suction cup; and take the wick as before, and restart it often, if you need. 
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup therefore which is administered in illness of pleuresin, on all sharp pain, has no handle nor piercing, and is administered only when it is full of water, and is put upon the member only so much; and this is the form: 
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leech wounds are introduced only in members where one cannot put suction cups because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar things; and in their denuded flesh, such as two or three, and others similar; and the qualities of the user is that when you find leeches that are in sweet water nets without purgation, if you take them; and put them one nut in sweet water, until they are famished, and have nothing in their bellies; and then it should be healed by vein and suction cup, then rub the member so much as it is red, and put on the leeches; and when they will be full, and fall off, if it is their place where one can put a suction cup, then put it, because it is worth much afterward. 
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If this is not done, lift the place of ease, and then with water, well, and then the strained. And if the place heals too much after the body of the wounds, moisten the linen cloth in cold water and put on top, as long as the wound is stretched; and if the wounds are multiplied, put on top crushed vitriol, or gall, and similar things, until it is stretched; or you put on the place half of peeled beans, and leave them as long as they dry on the place, so now will it stop; and if you need more, take other wounds. 
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the sinuses do not want to be taken, then rub the place with fresh blood, or insert a needle there until the sinuses are open, and then put them on top, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will harden; and when you see that they are bleeding, powder it with a little aloes and thyme crushed, or ash, they will now fall.  
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the fool who does not read from this chapter will never see anything from the ancient books, nor will he have read any of them; and for this reason, the science is estranged in our land, because I have never found anyone good; and I know nothing, except through the knowledge of the ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have shown you in this chapter what is contained, and I have abridged it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in these two chapters before. 
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore fitting that we say or prologue of this book the sums of the word and the chapters where the sages put their understanding, and stay on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient on one side and the other, if any thing does not allow it, such as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age; or if his tension is not very warm, or too cold; and avoid cold things, that is to say, cold dishes, and meat of hare and lamb, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with meats which fill the veins with blood, as long as you have doubt of a hot abscess, or spreading of matter in the limb; so the patient returns to his first government that he has used.  
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one nourish the patient with meats that make great nourishment, or he has viscosity, like wheat cooked in water, and rice, and testicles, and feet, and belly of calf, and eggs, and fresh fish, and thick wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with this nourishment they recover strength and more quickly the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the bones broken of the old and the decrepit do not well reunite or weld according to their nature for the dryness of the limbs, nor also those who are too tender, like the bones of little children; but make no cure, reset upon the broken bone the gross tendons which hold together and join the limb together, as long as it enforces as it was before; and not the least point of its work, and for this it is necessary to nourish them with thick meats, as we have said. 
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the leg, or of the thigh, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to the outside and others inward, like the point of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if with fracture, and fracture to a small split all.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And to each manner has its engine and its proper instrument in the restoration, according to what memory comes in its place; and is known the fracture of the bone by that which its parts are twisted, and it appears well by outside, and feels at the pressing of the hand; and when there is no torsion nor feel upon touching, and the patient does not feel much pain, if there is no fracture; but it may well have torsion, or fissure, or small fracture.  
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not advisable to move it with your hand, but apply the medications that come after here, and then restrain it gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture that goes in a bow, and are the two parts disjoined, it is necessary now to put them together equally, so that abscesses do not come; and if abscesses come, let him leave none for a day, until the abscess is quieted; then set it equal to the measure that you can easily and sagely, and know that the restoration of this one is easier than the restoration of him who has pieces; then restrain, as it is necessary afterwards. 
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone is broken in pieces, it is from two parts, whether it is hands or feet, or to your hand if it is a small limb, or to two cords, or to one cord and to your hand; and place the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken limb are freed, you straighten by all means the additions in their places as much as you can, and keep that by your work no lesion or pain comes to the patient; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms. 
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels it well in the hand if it seems to you that it is not well: if it is drawn beautifully and do not restrain it too much, nor press as those who make it come by their work abscesses hot and contraction to the limb, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, carefully instruct the patient that he not move it, neither watching nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other manner; and watch well that the limb be so assured that he feel no pain.  
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, except at the point, and it is necessary to put him in such a disposition that he does not feel any pain; and keep that he be put straight, so that tortuosity may not come when he is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you. 
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and in bigness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and similar things: it is necessary to wrap them in soft and fine linen cloths; and those that are large, such as hips and thighs: it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and hard bandage, because the wide bandages embrace the whole great limb, and restrain it from all sides equally, so that there is no gap; then bind light splints, III tours or IIII according to the limb, and tighten your hand a bit on the whole bandage, then go above the fracture and tighten less, so that the fracture then moves away a bit from the fracture; and soften the bandage bit by bit, until you reach most of the healthy part, then take the other splint, and turn it back upright on the fractured part; then return to the lower part of the fracture, and tighten it moderately, neither too hard nor too loosely, as we have said in the first place above; then put between the bandages splints of linen or cloth, until they are all equal, then tie everything from above with a bandage, and then put your well-made dressings on top, if there is no abscess or swelling. 
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is a swelling or abscess, put on top a soothing thing for the abscess hot, and which removes the swelling, and leave it so for some days; then strain on your temples, and be half an inch wide carefully cut, or from wood from which one makes the staffs, or from palm branches, and be according to this figure: 
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the splint that one puts on the fracture be a little larger and wider than the others; and also as long as it suits the limb in size or grandeur; then tighten on the splints as you have done at the first hour, then bind above with a thread evenly, as in the first hour on the fracture; tighter is on top, less; and it is necessary that the threads be medium, not too thick nor too fine, and be of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I want to do works from the fools who make their splints with cords of twisted flax, and this is a great error, because the splint cannot be equal if it is too thin, and it does not behoove that between each splint there be less than two fingers' width of space. 
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is chafed by the stitches after the tightening in their health, then put underneath them wadding of linen, or wool felt, so that it does not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the bone is broken, I shall say its cure here after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to straighten all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, it is not fitting to put splints for after V days or VII, or more according to your surety of the abscess happening; and see here the manner of the old plasters for restoring fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and that you take of flour that holds itself to the walls of the mill, and you confis it with abundance of egg, and put this confection, not too light nor too thick, and in use, and this is the common manner of the plaster restoring the fracture to many dispositions, and even to women and to small children, because it is not too hot nor too cold.  
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restoring fractures and dislocations and torsions: take  three parts each of abarris, ladani, enula, asafoetida and gum arabic, and mugwort, ana .x. З.; myrrh and aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; and make it into a powder, and mix it with the white of an egg; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, because it is of good composition, and restores broken bones well, and is good for many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of emplasters that is good for torsion: take mugwort and viscidum, ana 10; mirr and aloes, ana 9; acaice 6; bolic armenic 10, and grind well, and confit with water or the white of an egg, and administer it.  
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another manner of emplastering joints and bones dislocated from their places, and calming the pain occurring, and the size used of bone, and the fracture: take new linen, and moisten it in water and oil cooked, and put it upon the place. 
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore, but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and removes pain properly. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way of making a plaster that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves, and ground ivy leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another manner of plaister for the restoration of broken bone and to lessen the remaining abscess. 
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of wormwood, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of verbena, one part each; and grind it, and confit with wine, and if the limb is chilled, confit it with moist coriander water, or water, and use it. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another manner of setting more forcefully than the first, when an abscess comes to the restoration of the limb. 
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the roots of vismalve, and seeds of flax, balsam, melilot, and sneezeweed, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of all one part; and grind, and confit with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest. 
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras says in his book that one should not put on the broken limb for restoration other than what is made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and says it should be between two, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen that one must put on the broken limb, to restore, things dry a little hot, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of making a plaster that is good for the lesion and pain: take mugwort and chaff of sheep's wool cut, or feathers of eyes, and marsh mallow, and seal evenly, and grind them, and make a plaster from it and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then after a while, untie it carefully and watch that the patient feels no pain, or if the bone has moved from its place; if not, do not untie it for many days. And if pain comes to the place, or itching, lack of rest or swelling, hurry, and untie it and remove the bandage now; and take a light cloth, and a sponge of moist sea water, and dip in water, and raise the area, until the itching ceases and the pain is appeased; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on a dry linen cloth, moistened in water or rose oil, and tie over it a nut, as long as you are sure of a warm abscess; and rest the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then begin again the subtle bandage, and a little of the bandage, and do not restrain it as tightly as before; and continue until it is healed. 
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and pain and swelling are completely gone, and you need plaster and bandage, then begin again as you did first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb anything of what we have said, if it is not untied after III days or IIII or V or VII; and no time leaves XX days, according to what one sees, as long as the fracture heals, and approaches the joining of the bone above; then you restrain it more than before, and the fat thickens its flesh, as I said before; and if you see it drying more than is necessary, know that nourishment cannot come; arose then of warm water bathe, all the time that you untie it, and this be every third day, and loosen a little the bandage; by this work therefore shortens the inflammation of the limb, and repairs quickly what do the foolish mire, who keep the limb twisted: this is bad, and so is works fearful, and I see nothing else than to leave it and work it straight. 
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many ways of fractures and diverse figures, and the causes are determined; for there are fractures that are made by the percussion of a sword, and the collarbone breaks all the bone up to the place which is below the bone, like it is done with a haiche or a staff; and because of this, this kind of fracture is called "haichure". 
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword cuts the bone from above without piercing, and this kind of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an impact embedded, or a fissure or of the neck of the bone, or of the head on the bone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture passing, which approaches to the membrane that is under the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is either great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound which is put back into the bone as subtly as a thread, and is the fissure small, and for this reason this fracture is called 'capillary'; and if the wound which is made either by striking with stone, or by falling, or by similar thing, and makes enter the piece of the bone down, and is the leus like how make the blacksmith when it forge on the cauldrons; so enters the stone within. 
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have or whose bones are moist, such as children's heads; and it happens in all these ways of breakage that small pieces are dislodged from them like stars; and I will speak of them in their place. 
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all the ways of fractures by the subtraction on them, and the inquiry at tents, and by the rotten flesh which is on top.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the capillary blood vessel is known by this: when one has discovered the bone and rubs it, black breakage appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure of the fracture, take care of the accidents of the sick person, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of phlegm, and loss of understanding, and extension, and swelling, and fever ague, and the eyes being watery and red, and other similar things in more dispositions, then he cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an unfavorable accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture first comes to you, and it is in winter, then it behooves to remove the bone before the fourteenth day as much as you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the flesh beneath the bone may not rot, and come the accident that we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes to the cloth that covers the brain, then it is necessary that you split the broken part thus: and it is that you prick the head of the patient carefully, and uncover on the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the figure of the wound more gently than you can, and if bleeding comes when uncovering the bone, or abscess applies, help him with what he needs, and it is that you fill the place with soft cloths soaked in rose oil; and make the wound rest until the abscess applied is calmed, and be assured of bleeding; then begin to remove the bone around, and it is done according to two ways of work: one way is that you cut along a narrow strip in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then put another incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have a number of incisions of different sizes, some narrow and others wide, sharp at one end, and made of iron; and in working lightly, so that you do not pierce the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is broken and hard, it is necessary that you pierce it through, so that you administer splints with tarteres, not too deeply so that they do not go beyond the bone of the test, and it must have above the point a margin or circle, that does not let pass the point beyond the bone; and you should have more than one, so that each comes in its place from the thickness of the bone, so that you have splints for all tests; and this is the form of the three types of tarretes:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing through the broken bone is that you put one tarrete on the bone, and turn to your two until you know that the bone is pierced; then put the tarere back in another place a little after, and thus do all around, then cut with incisors the space of the bone which is between the perforations, and do this more subtly as you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as tweezers, pliers; and guard that you do not touch the brain nor the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you will have the bone pierced, and treated, it is necessary that you reset the pointed tool which is lodged from the bone to all other instruments seeming to a scalpel, but it is necessary that it be more hardened and more subtle than the other scalpel; and if it remains nothing of the little bones, or no scales, then cure the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.  
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of working is this one that Galen says, which is drier; and he praises it greatly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a portion of the bone where the broken part appears, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place underneath the head of this lentil-shaped incisional instrument, for this is its shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and let the part be sharp in two sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so that you lightly break the bone all around, and take good care of the cloth that is underneath; if it is attached to the bone, gently remove it, because it is removed well without pain, and without fear. 
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the broken bone does not pierce to the skin, and the bone is cut only from above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to reassemble that sprain, and remove the scales with a fine razor which you must have in various quantities, so as to administer in each place the most suitable one, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you start with large razors, and then smaller ones after that, and do not cease doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other capillary and subtle cuts, it is necessary that you administer care according to its location; and this thing is not well-answered by him who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the wound is uncovered, it is necessary that you take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and put it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and put it on the first cloth; and do this more lightly than you can, that you do not hurt the wound; then administer above a bandage, and do not constrain it more than so that it holds the wound only; and let it be like that for a day or two, until the pus has calmed down; then untie it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, and poppy flour, and incense powder, and wormwood, and similar things; and of these things make powder, and put on the wound, and administer additional unctionless medicines; and guard that the wound is always clean, that you do not leave any ointment, nor let it gather pus, for when pus gathers on the brain tissue, it corrupts and harms, and brings great evil to the patient; because when one puts a pungent thing on the wound, it stings upwards.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take guard then, if no bad accidents come to the patient, as we have said, so is it doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blackening does not come forth except for the medicine that has been put on it, which it has virtue, then it is necessary that you take a part of honey, and III parts of rose oil, and glue I cloth, and put it on the sore; then cure it in ways of cures that are fitting, until it be healed. 
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the two bones above are broken, or one by itself, because they are two bones; and the lower one is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it is forced or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you put your small finger or pierced through the nails, and put each fracture inside your index finger, and to the pouch outward, until the nails return according to its natural figure; and do this gently, and guard that the patient does not feel pain from your work. 
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper part of the leg and the bone cannot come to its place, then it is necessary that you put it even at the head of a stick a little thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is of two parts, make another one like it, and hasten to restore the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the abscess has calmed, then bind to the head with two layers of linen cloth, if the fracture is in one part. 
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bandage one on the other side, if the fracture is there; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the hollows of the leg.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say one must moisten the tents with butter, and change them every day. 
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that they be softened in the preparation of aubun from an egg, and powdered with millet; then let the tent remain, until the bones are hard, and the cartilages hardened.  
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one puts goose feathers in their place, and if so, a single piece of cloth is draped over, and the bandage stays put, and it blows on the patient; do whatever you want.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the new while you are working on it, then put a cloth or cotton moistened in rose oil, or in a teaspoon of diaquilon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses do not come, if you put a poultice from afar, of sesame flour, and incense powder, mixed with egg white, then put light compresses on top, and do not bind it at all; and if the break of the bone is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then extract them with suitable instruments to that, then sew the crack, and cure it with things bringing flesh, and soldering, as are poultices and ointments suitable to that; and if inside there is no wound whatsoever, then cure it with tents, and put twigs of splint inside, until it is healed. 
de la routure de la mandibule	of the jaw fracture
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken below, and there is no wound outside, and the fracture is outside only so much, and is not broken in two, except for the cartilage inside, if one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right part, that you put your index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left jaw, then put your index finger from the right hand, and push the fracture inward lightly, and hold it with the other hand outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jaw fracture is dislocated into two parts, it is necessary that you administer extension of two parts, until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth occurs, or a break, then restrain with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place on the broken jaw cerote, and place on it one double drapel; and place on the drapel a large star well made, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it up as much as you can, and command the patient to rest, and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then untie it on the third day, and then put back in place what has changed; and put a plaster on top, of powder from the mill with abundance of egg or flaxseed flour, after you have removed the cerote; and put a light linen cloth over the plaster, and if the plasters dries, and the patient’s disposition does not change, leave it as long as it is healthy; many times it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, then administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, reward none of the bone pieces are removed; so subtly remove them with instruments suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there is none remaining, then close the wound if it is wide, and put on one suitable plaster for this purpose, to prevent flesh from forming, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fracture breaks many times in front, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is in three ways: or it is broken and separated into two, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is like this when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the shoulder which is the fractured bone; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then put each fracture to your hands, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, put under the shoulder of the patient a round ball of cloth, or wool, and be as large as your need; and gently lift the bone, and tighten the ball with your hand, so that you put each fracture together as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the forceps out by force because it comes embedded, then it is necessary that the patient lie often on his back, and put under the shoulder one oreillier in the middle, and push the ministers' shoulder down, until the bone of the forceps is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then address the fracture to your two [hands], and if you find it shattered, then it is necessary that you split it up; and treat the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join for any elevation, then cut with one of the incisors that you have; but that you put under the forceps this instrument, to guard the syfac.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it seems like a spoon, and is not hollow, and be as wide as it is convenient, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have it two ends, as you see, and let one be wide, and the other narrow, as it is the rupture of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are assured of a hot abscess, so close the wound, and if the rupture is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, so cover the wound with bandages and tents, according to its quantity. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes, then moisten one cloth in rose oil and honey and wine, and put it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The straining of the bone, when it is sensed in wounds and in incisions, is that you put on the bone the plaster of the powder of mill and of yolk of egg, and put light compresses on top, and put a spear under the saddle, if you have need of it; then take a very broad band of a palm wide, then put the double drape on top of the compresses, and the plaster; then take a thin strip of III fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the head of the bandage hangs down; and put the strip on the fracture, and turn the bandage up on the neck, and under the good saddle, and under the bad saddle; and tighten each side, and when you see that the splint holds the fracture well, and you clearly see that the strip does not move above the broken bone, so you reinforce it every day, and when the ligaments loosen, then you restrain it; and make the patient lie on his back, and put him when he sleeps a small pillow under the saddle, to raise the shoulder up; so will lighten the fracture of the force by the elevation of the shoulder, or you bind his arm to the neck, and do not release it unless bad accidents come to it, until XX days; then restart the plaster, if you see that he has need of it, and restrain and leave it as it is, until it is restored; and it is restored in the most within XXVIII days, and in less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Sometimes the shoulder breaks or dislocates in its middle and only feels it by touch; so, according to the figure of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural form, in all the ways that you can; then put on the place powder of the mill with abundance of egg, and light bandages, and put above a double cloth; then put above a wide and thin splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and if the splint is rough anywhere on the shoulder, so take that roughness of linen bandages, so that the splint rests evenly; and then restrain it with a very tight bandage, so that the splint does not move from its place, and look at the limb every day; and all times that it softens, so restrain it, and put back in place the splint if it is out of place, and lie the patient on his side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 days or in 25, and when this number is completed, then untie it, and be sure, because it is not a bone that easily moves out of place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone sticks out ahead and not under the heart, so do it above, and the bone, and do what we have said in the fracture of the arm to soothe abscess hot.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it often breaks at the end. 
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, so it declines to the outside, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of strength, and weakness, and perhaps vomits blood, and opens the veins on the broken bone, and he smells good. 
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back, and put one cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders together, and he brings the sides of the two bones together with your hands, and carefully try to set them in every way as much as you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then put plasters and bandages over the fine skin, or a light cloth such as gauze, and wrap it in one bandage, and tie it above the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turn the band around to the back, and tighten it evenly, and reward each hour the patient’s limb, and if it softens, tighten it; and if it is necessary to untie it, because of corrosion or itching which comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hasten, and untie it, and wipe the plaster away, and treat what has come there in ways of cure; then put back the plaster, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs comes only in their thick parts after the back, and at the top inside, and they bend only for that reason because they are brittle; and one feels it well upon inquiry to both sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you put the fracture equal, as it is fitting. 
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then place the splint, and restrain it with a strap, if you need it. 
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breaking of ribs is declining inwards, the patient feels very great pain and sharp pain, as well as from pleurisy, because the bone pricks the membrane; and besides pains, and coughs and vomits a large planty of blood, and it is of grievous health, and the ancients have placed great importance upon it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say it is necessary to administer meats that swell the belly, to drive out the wind.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, except for hot abscesses if they have not yet come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say none of us put suction cups on the place to suck out fluid, and that seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the suction cups draw out the superfluities to the place for the disposition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said to you of which one must cover the place with soft wool in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to make equal the layer around, then be cured from the cure of pleurisy, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain which he cannot endure from the bone that pierces the flesh, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut on the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put under it an instrument to guard the skin; and afterwards one must saw through the bone, and scrape gently, and then stitch the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with ointments, until it is healed.  
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, put on it soft cloths in rose oil, and put on the top; and care while the place of this one that it befits the abscess, and lie sideways on his side where it should be, until it is healed. 
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is a fracture of the bones of the neck, and it happens that it bends; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, take note if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and he cannot move them nor extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many dispositions, and if they move and feel well when they are pulled and held, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if one takes care of it. 
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things happen to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healthy or not, then take ward if the limbs are softened, and if the accidents are in the hands, and on the back there is a sauteness and egestion without will; and when one has laid it on its stomach, there is an egestion without will.  
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is placed on its back and wants to sit up, it cannot. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal; if he does not labor in its care. 
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, then the thing is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you reheat it if there is an abscess, then put on the spine rose oil or oil of egg yolk, until it is soothed; then put on a comforting and drying plaster, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels the pain, as long as he is well.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is dislocated, it is necessary to cover the wound; and remove the bone, then assemble the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then cure it with ointment that promotes healing, until it is well; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow", then you put your fist of your left hand in there, and put it equal to the other hand as best you can, then put the plaster and bandage on top, if you need it; then restrain it, and if there are dislocated bones, do this again, remove the bone, and cure the wound until it is well.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.
