Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And that you put II  sticks to the head of the patient of an arm of great, and towards the feet II others, and have between each stick, up and down, a palm's width of long; and have in each stick I hole, where the string goes, and be the sticks firmly in the earth so that they do not move; and between each II sticks have I turning stick, for which the thread turns, and have in II turning II small sticks of a palm long, to turn the turning; and then tie the string that is among the handles to the turning towards the head, and the other string towards the feet to the other turning, and each of the ministers turns his turning to the whole string, and the master puts the spine equal as we have said. 
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is equal, put a drying plaster with an abundance of egg, and then the bandages, and then the splint of a tablet of three two of long, that covers the place of the gibbosity and the part of the healthy spine, then tie it with a bandage, as we have said, and use the patient of subtle nourishment, until he is healed; and if any thing comes in the end of the health, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the splint that we have said before; and sometimes one administers a piece of wood, and sometimes the appearance comes in the back spine of the back, and they think that this is dislocations; and this is the bone that opens, therefore one should not have presumption: perhaps it would bring death. 
des dislocations de la hainche	of the hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder come out only through dislocations, and not like other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to .iiij. parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more inside then, and a little dislocated front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and opens more the knee of the sick person than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot double his knee to the fire; and is the part which is below swollen with hot abscess, because the head of the hip comes there. 
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes in fever, is that this accident is contrary to these before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of him to whom it happens in front, is that his leg is well aligned according to its completion; however, he does not bend his knee without pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot before, and he retains his urine, and swells his groin, and when he goes, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of him to whom it happens behind, is that he cannot spread his knee nor bend it, and his leg is more twisted than the other, and his groin is softened, and the head of the hip bone is in its place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The treatment of this kind of dislocation is that you regard whether the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its disposition, then there is no need for cure; and there is no need for him to have presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those whose dislocation is fresh, and it's of .iiij. manners of dislocation, so haste that you return the joint, and the extension inside and outside, and the movement to right and left; perchance it will return, and has no need of other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must appear as the minister strong, and hold the leg strong with two hands, or at the limb that is tied above the knee; and another minister stretches his hand above in such a manner that he puts his hands below his shoulders, then tightens with a linen cloth above the hip; and another holds the chief of the limb; and extend upwards and downwards all at once, until the patient is lifted from the ground at one time, and remains suspended.  
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four appearances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If this is not the case, it is necessary to take care of its appearance. When the dislocation is at the shoulder, you should put the patient on his healthy side, then place the linen on the base of the hip, and the place which is below the groin, then extend the linen upwards towards the groin and towards the force; then grab some other ministers with his arms, and embrace the large part of the diseased hip, and extend it outwards in a straight line: now it will return to its place; and this way of dislocation is lighter than others.  
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tighten it in this manner that we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong rope over the two heels, and over the two knees, and let the injured leg be extended two finger lengths more than the other; then let it be hung from the top of a pole, and let it be two arm lengths above the ground; then command the minister that he embrace the head of the hip, and let another minister hang with the patient who embraces the hip tightly, for now the joint returns easily. 
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is at the rear, he lies the patient as we have said in the one who has glibosity, and restrains I liien upon the bad leg properly, and upon the foot also; then puts II sticks, I at the chief and I other at the feet, then puts I stick between the hips of the sick emmi the form; and ait planty of moist cloths around, that it does not bleed him the patient, then extends each minister toward him, and he sets the dislocation equal to his hand. 
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.  
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place him on a.i.e., table, and press him as we have said in the book of the chapter, and lie the patient on his healthy side. 
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the leg as much as possible and according to what I have said; and put his pain to be on the injured limb, then press with the other hand, and bring the end towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in the hip, it is not necessary to stretch the patient down or raise him up on the ground, but he must be as if the hip was dislocated outward, as we have said about the laying down on the two hips; and be upon his face, and the band stretched as we have said before, and one must press upon the joint to the table; and it will be in point when the patient stretches his legs, and they will be equal; then adjust the thighs, and put the splint, and the strain of a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and let him rest III days or IV, then untie, and put the splint on top; and if you see that they are equal, strain it, as before, and leave it III days; then untie, and allow it to go well, until the limb is strengthened. 
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inside and outside, and behind; and it does not dislocate in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg to his hip, and if it does not rest at his hip, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back on his waist, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and draw it between your thighs, then bend the two bones that form the knee; and other ministers extend his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it rests gently his leg at his hip; and put the plaster on, and make the leg rest at the hip, and bind them together strongly for III days or IIII, then untie it; and do not let the patient work to go, as long as the limb is strengthened.  
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not straight, administer strong extension, as we have said in the cure of the hip, until it is healed. 
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels is sometimes sprained, and sometimes dislocated completely, inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and tender before the part where it is dislocated; the reduction is light, and one must extend it gently with his hands when it is only eased. 
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated from the whole, you must have the patient sit straight, and hold him by the legs, above the ankle; then pull the foot to you with your right hand, and then with your left two times, then up to the top, and push the foot well upward; and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, it is good; if not, begin the work again, for it will return; and if it cannot return thus, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and put the post firmly in the ground between his hips, and tie blankets around him so that he does not get cold; then hold the patient by the hip, and some other ministers extend the foot to their hands or to the ligature, so that they tie it above the ankle of the foot; then stretch each minister equally, and the post should be well between the hips of the patient to keep the patient when he is extended; then put your hands on the dislocation, and some other ministers hold the sound leg below, and the dislocation will return easily.  
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is pointed, place the plaster and bandages on top, and strain them firmly, and bind his leg to the leg, and guard the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the bandage is not too tight; then leave him II days or III, and if the bandage softens, strain it again. Then unbind it after the third day or fourth, and forbid the patient from walking for IIII days; and if he goes before that time limit, it is not certain that he will not dislocate it again. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to this place, then you must soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the hips are dislocated, it is fitting to extend them well without effort, and this is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the back of the foot, it behooves you to make the patient sit on a flat place or on a table straightly, and put your foot on what opens of these joints, then press with your foot firmly, until it returns; and when it is equalized, and there is nothing open, so put under the sole of the foot a table at the shoulder, then constrain it firmly, and leave it for III days, then untie it; and make him rest, until he is healed. 
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies: so be not presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it long, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and tardy, nor bold; and use at the beginning of calming things abscess hot, and leave the patient in the hands of God, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, so reset now the limb to its place, as well as the abscess heals there; and when the limb is in its place, administer calming things abscess hot, and cure the wound, as it befits, with dressings dry; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are displaced, set them, and do what we have said in simple illnesses; and keep yourself from entering into a way of fear, according to what I have said, for this brings you death according to your Creator, and for the safety of your weapon and your body.
